O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine by assembling its filling, and have made its end through his explanations and by his declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to my vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is strongly rooted in our region and has been entirely excluded from everything, the science has perished and been cut off, and nothing remains except the small descriptions in books by the ancients that their hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came errors and vanities, and the intentions have been closed, and the science has been neglected.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I should vitalize the entire arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and will assemble the forms of the cautery irons, and other tools of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no skilled surgeons are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting that he who undertakes this master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and blood vessels and the number of them, and their movements and veins moving and resting, and from where they issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And because Hippocrates said that without understanding is much, and without practice is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of manual skills.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned should beware lest he act improperly and harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	So many times I have wished more of those who undertake this science and abandon themselves to it without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I have seen a fool who incised an abscess of scrophules or throat of a woman, and incised the arteries of her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	for so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I have seen another fool who incised a stone from an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	and he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to draw the stone, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I have seen another fool who took care of the Duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the burner made a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the surgeons full of ignorance restrain the breakage on the wound with strong ligatures, and do not leave any part of the flesh untied, and leave it thus completed.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commands that he does not release it at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and he delays until the leg becomes entirely swollen and the foot rots away.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and hastened to come to release the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I heard him dislocate it, he was at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But the corruption of the bone was already confirmed or in the member, and could not be cured.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the member was entirely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And take another blade which collapses the embedded abscess, and then inflame through the wickedness of its authority.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For an abscess, when it is pure of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron if it is not in such a place where all the corrupted parts can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this, dear son, you need to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in many positions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this, it is necessary that you take care of it, so that the foolish ones cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your instruments in hand and approach your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way, so that by the grace of God you come to their salvation and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the terrible diseases threatening health;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your arms from that which causes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take ill diseases into your care if you are to be called mad.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have dealt with this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and water medicament cauteries, and are ordered from the head down to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the forms of the instruments, and the implements for the cautery, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it is about the chapters ordered and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about resetting dislocations and twists, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the shoulder to the feet, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, since we remember the work, it must be that I describe the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of the aid, and of harm, are the longest discourse and subtle science and the secrets replied to.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and on this many wise men spoke, and agreed with it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and let them speak but little, for I fear the lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the fire cautery helps universally in all complexions where there is matter, whether of two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say complexion warm with matter, and dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a warm and dry complexion with matter, they debated and said that the fire cautery is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that the fire cautery is not useful for a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be applied to a warm disease by heat, nor by dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he says who says the opposite that the fire cautery does great help for sickness hot and dry that comes in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of the man and his moisture according to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it so through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in all cases, do not intervene unless it is someone who has proven its effectiveness and knows through long practice the art of cauteries, and the diversity of human constitutions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and duration of the time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other constitutions we have no fear, especially for cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the more they came together and agreed on the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery together with heat is of the secrets of wound treatment, and has greater goodness than a burning medicinal cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and affects only the part that is burned, and does not harm other parts to a great extent.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Hot medicines spread from one part to another and cause diseases in the affected parts due to their heat.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and sometimes they cure the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experience and the length of service and study I have devoted to the art, and it is concerning the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse the length of the words, for it pleases me not to deprive you of the secret, which is about the fire and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher states in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, boy, when the cauteries ought to be made, and they have chosen times.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that the fire cautery is suitable at all times, for the evils coming about are removed by the aid of the cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially if the cautery is for pains urgent and necessary that cannot wait for the time when greater mischief does not arise in the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think of it, dear boy, as those foolish men do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, for cautery is not medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humors that cause pain, and it works like medicine for the speed of its virtue and the power and authority of its action.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease comes once according to the patient's constitution and the location of the disease and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and they are gathered in him due to the acquisition of meats and similar things, if not, apply cauteries to him where there is little excess and moisture, as with cauteries for pain, and similar things, and the same pain will not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And few people understand for what reason cauteries are called the last of medicine, and this is true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauteries work after medicine, and their belief is false. For when we administer methods of treatment for any disease and they do not work, then we apply the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauterization is the latest in medicine, not according to the intention of wise men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cautery instruments made of gold are hotter than those made of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of the gold or its high density;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the coals of the cautery do not cause putrefaction, but this is not true because I have proven it and found that it is indeed true in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cautery instruments are hotter than those made of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And whenever you heat an instrument made of gold, you cannot tell when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it will cool quickly.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if you heat it too much;
si font au feu;	if they do it with fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and then there is sufficient obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter from the head to the feet, because the veins should be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold in the head, and there are two of them, which we make because of a disease called "soda," and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for the multitude of dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by medicinal means changing the humor three or four times, according to what the virtues and strength of the liquid and the custom of the patient allow.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then reapply the cautery to the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then place it crosswise in your hands, and put his hands on the palms;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after place the base of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and when these two means come, bleed from the armpit then heat the cautery called "olive", of which here is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the armpit mark with ink, and do so by lowering and withdrawing your hand little by little, turning it.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then withdraw your hand alone, and raise the armpit if you see bone slightly.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	after take some thread, and put in soft cotton inside, and place it on the armpit, and let it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after apply a moistened cloth to it in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and keep it there until the cauterization is removed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after apply the ointment called "tetrapharmacos" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges.
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, apply herbs.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And any of them said that the fire cautery should be applied so much that part of the bone is burned, and then the burned part of the bone should be removed and cleaned.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And another says that the cauterization should be left on until it blisters, and to apply it so strongly that it causes a blister as wide as the comb that women use in their hairpins, for this causes the fluids to move out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must keep the wound widely open;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after which one must treat and dress.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem entirely good in all respects, except for those who have a way to fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should let the fire cautery alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the shoulders are weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we testify in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the patient's shoulders are weak by nature, and the first application of the fire cautery seems more helpful and soothing to me, and from that I work in this assembly for healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in the entire body there comes chronic pain that lasts long, the patient should use years and pills called "cochie" and purgatives of head and eyes and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if we apply the fire cautery as we have said before, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the sick person is of strong nature, and that it not be too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then the cautery should be applied over that cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After apply the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and apply the cautery or reset called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and this is where one places cups;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lift your hand so that it does not reach the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the cautery for the horns should be finer than that used for the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	for the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When there is sudden pain in a part of the head, and the disease extends to the eye, and the shoulder is cleansed with purgative medicines, and other treatments for the condition have been performed as I described in the division of diseases, and all this does not help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then he makes cauterizations according to two methods, that is to say from aqueous medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauterization from aqueous medicine is that you take a decoction of aloes, and peel off the bark and rind just a little around two shoulders, and then apply the decoction underneath the skin in the area where the pain resides.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is applied, it should be pressed well and left thus for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then remove the bandage and apply a dressing of garlic decoction, and leave the wound for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then place on a cloth soaked in butter until it dries out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the ointment treatment until he is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that he uses some of the burning medicines that I have written or in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron cautery using coal; it has the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a clove or it has little curvature, and in the middle there is a small appearance.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and gently turn the flesh a bit until the halves of the core of the wound are burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is above, and allow an abundance of blood to flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After apply cotton for the sake of the thread, put on the head for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I put wet cotton in butter, and then treat the head with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you wish to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare," do it entirely around the edge, and be careful not to burn the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of emigraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat the headache as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterization previously mentioned from medicine and of iron is not sufficient, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white-hot;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and thus stretch over the bone a line of half a digit in length, and take your hand once, hold that so as not to compress the artery and not to come until the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and watch the mandible that moves when we eat, and the nerves so they look only at the move and that spasm does not arise in the patient, and watch for bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or bleeding has great fear and especially to those who do not know it, and are untrained.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work proceed in its course;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop the blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see, administer the cautery as we have said or chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery having two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better and more effective than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and you have applied medicinal solutions and other treatments as we have said in the division, and the pains do not change, then heat this cautery called "poins," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncturing all around the affected ear, or around both sides where the pain is felt, and then move a little bit upwards from the root of the ear after marking the area.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and have X points between each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the wound is cleaned until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be cured by fire cautery is not those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make any fire cautery for those that come from drying and fainting of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this form of torture that moves from phlegm in the fluids and purgatives of bile and gargling, and if it is ineffective, then you must cauterize the patient with three fire cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	One at the root of the ear, and the other a little above the temple, and the third in the alignment of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the healthy part that opens, and apply the cautery over a little above the tip of the ear, and another one on the temple as long as an inch;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery there until the muscles of the heart are burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is the shape of the cautery that we placed before, but it is a bit more subtle, and it should be that the knives are a bit larger.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of the wound as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When the apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then I apply four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	On the two horns of the head, and one on the head, and one on the area called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the opening of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	For lithargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this disease, give the patient large and purgative pills for cleansing the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after resetting the patient's head, and placing it on the occiput, apply the mustard plaster described or treated in the section on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the way of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it is done thus, well done;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it is not done thus, apply three cauteries down the back from the neck to the collarbone, with an inch of space between each cautery.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat the wound as with others, and if you see fit to adjust it, and the patient is suffering, apply one cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the task is, two others on the two horns, and treat until it is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery which is called "olivare," as I have said before, be present.
de la froidor dou chief	from the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of pus and what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after clean the head of the patient, then heat the head of the patient, and apply the cautery through the head and on each horn, and the fourth and third on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you have more need of it, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease is severe, then apply four cautery marks on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let them [the cautery] remain until the pain is less, and remove your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until it is healed, and use the cautery called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use fire cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain with years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the patients are great and suffer from gentle medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is an infant who cannot bear the pain, have them perform gargling and chewing, frequently modifying the mixture with good meats.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after placing the king in the middle, and apply the cautery as we have said before, and on the vessel, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and in great pain, apply the cautery as I have said for those with paralysis and muscle weakness, on the spine of the back and neck, and use the olive cautery as I described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is injured, if he undergoes the fine cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause of melancholy is corrupt superfluities or thick phlegm, then the cautery with such cauteries as we have said for paralysis should be used.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities are declining into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink things by which his brain may be purified, according to those described earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After reduce the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after make the ligature of linen well done, like a circle, and put it around the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient lies stretched out, and be well held from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after present the ligature, and apply it with old goat's butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat the iron well, so that the doze can be applied as long as it can be endured;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after empty the circle from within through the head, and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once each week with another better regimen until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see to cauterize him, make pricks in several places throughout the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain greatly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then place soft cotton soaked in butter and gelatin fat on it.
de l’awe des eulz	from the fear of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When fear comes first to the eyes through the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and have the patient drink things that cleanse the head, and protect him from all moisture, and make him sweat or take baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After this, instruct him to turn his head, and apply a cautery under the chin, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the downward movements of the jaw are together with the eyes, or in one if the movement is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cover the entire area of the cautery with all the veins and arteries beneath the ear, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood come out, stop it with the same method you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of the arteries and in the incision how to handle it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And once done, cauterize or treat the two hindmost bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the chest due to tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed to be on the veins, or drain the arteries that are visible at the back of the head.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and when it is seen that they are cold phlegmatic excesses, then I do the cauterization that I said at the beginning of this work descending to the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cauterize at the back of the head, and two cauterizations above the two temples, and two cauterizations or treat the two hindmost bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is need for more, cauterize the bleeding from the sorcery with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	with the body of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit the patient, then give the patient three noxious pigs to drink;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after you set the head, and do a cauterization or in the middle of the olive cauterization;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and do two cauterizations of the cauterization called "clavilis" above the two pigs, a little below the eyebrows;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery so you do not burn it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which here is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, make two fire cauteries above the two sinews as long as the sinews are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and leave your hand there until the third part of the paper be burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair which points to the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes the hairs of the eyes turn to white teeth, and prick the eye, and then one makes fire cauteries according to two manners:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are equal, then put the patient in a sound state;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after marking on the paper the eyes, draw a figure that be as much like the leaf of the laurel, and be the beginning of the sign among the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put moist cotton in egg white and myrtle wax on the eye, then heat the cautery as described by its form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterize on the figure you have marked, do so only a little bit many times, until the corners are scorched in place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of health of the work are that you see the paper withdrawn, and the hairs raised to the outline of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then gently hold your hand, and let it be thus for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burning is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the application of ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if hairs come after this, and the paper is softened, then resume the fire cautery in that same place, as you have done first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are removed, then cauterize until the paper lifts to its natural place and remains even, and do not prick the hairs near the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The fire cauterization in medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even, then make parchment in the shape of the leaf of juniper.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take of French soap and strong heat, of each one .Z., and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it quickly, so that it does not cool, then apply it to the form as you made it like the leaf of juniper, and place on the paper of eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease is only in the eye, one must open it, and if it is in both as well;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place moist cotton from an egg white over the eye;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the head of the patient be in a good position and place your hand showing over the medicine, and press it slightly and the egg each time the patient feels the medicine biting, for they feel the bite as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your duty.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the swelling has passed, lift the limb from rest, and reward if you see the paper lifted as if it were lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, apply the medicine to the limb again or until your treatment shows results, and keep your eyes focused.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place soft cloth with butter on it until the wound is healed, after which dress the limb with ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until he is cured.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to watch your work well with great care so that it does not fail in the application of the medicine.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft after, and the hair pricks in the eye, resume the treatment on that limb which is softened by the paper, as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment until he is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and it is the form of the leaf of the myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that men's eyes vary in size and smallness, and according to this, your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not follow the right way for him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	For the treatment of fistula by fire cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	instruct the patient to place his head on your side;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, nor his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after, place woolen cloth in the white of an egg or in the juice of pomegranate on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heating the cautery which is divided:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is placed on the shoulder in the shape of an arrow feather, ensuring that the cautery fits.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one shoulder to the other, and if you see, it should be like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but in any case, what is placed should move for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	after press the fistula if it is open, and drain the pus, and dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, work on it, and drain from the bowel.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after placing the hot cautery, hold your hand at the part above the neck next to the eye, so that your hand does not do foolish things;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, repeat the application of the cautery once more, and do this if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	afterwards, place moist cotton soaked in butter on it, and continue the application of the drying ointment until it is healed. If forty days pass and it is not healed, apply a watery corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and follow the king's instruction according to what he has written in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Hear about fistula, and set it right;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after insert the fine wax thread of hemp into the opening to shape it:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make it with the quantity of a .3. drop;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or the thread firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the melted wax does not flow into their eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to place over the eye a wet piece of cotton or from an egg:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the wax seals the fistula, and the healthy part with marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if not, it is fitting to administer pertusin to the neck, and bring the fistula back to the body of the neck according to what is proper in itself.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur in lips called "poil," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When the cure for these cracks, as we said in divisions, does not help, then heat the small fire cautery knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And place it quickly into those cracks until it comes to the surface;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after dress the wound until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the eye socket, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after performing putrefaction and drilling and it has healed and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, but it will not profit much:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must have the fire cautery according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the bottle or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron comes to the bottom of it, and beyond it;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so once or twice after the treatment as described in our treatments until he is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, that is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, you must expose the joint and remove the corrupt bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	by movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and it does not help, then place the patient's healthy side in the affected area.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery as described later in such a manner that you place a cane on the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and insert the hot cautery quickly inside, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after removing your hand, reapply the cautery as you see fit;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after make the patient lick salt water, and for the scabies, one hour and thoroughly dry.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a manner, the tooth that was moving is fixed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When pain in the teeth comes from cold or there is cold present, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use the cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and the butter cautery and the fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	The butter cautery is such that you take butter from a cow, and the end of it in a iron or tin spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after take cotton and wrap on the tip of a tent, and the marrow in butter boiled, and put on the tooth hurting quickly and hold until it be cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and so do often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see soft wool and cotton in cold butter, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the iron hot until the fire comes to the healing of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cauterizes as such that you take a steel or iron needle, and let it be large so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	after heat the cauterizer, of which the form will come next, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer be cooled;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be removed on that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And the patient should fill his mouth with good butter in anticipation of that cautery, and then quickly apply it.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make the cautery where you wish, and according to what you have power to do.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of gland swellings
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are of phlegm and cold moisture, and do not yield to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as described below. Let it have two openings for the vapors to escape from the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and apply the hot cautery to the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the center of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply moist cotton soaked in butter until the burn is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards apply ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moist humors overcome the channels of the body, and especially when this comes from a cold temperament, then it is necessary to first evacuate the patient with soluble medicines.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after you apply the cautery to the root of the throat, and make sure that you do not come too close to the throat, but do heat the heart a little bit, just a bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After, apply the other cautery to the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and let the cauteries which are called "clavile" be as we have shown their form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cauterization
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and the disease of the bowel is due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever and does not dry up, and the disease is old, apply two cauteries on the flank in their armpits;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and for another cautery place the point between the two mamels;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery that is called "clavile" be according to the form that is said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, make a cautery by pricking the entire area called "poins" whose form is described earlier in the disease of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the "poins" be up to XXX, or nearby.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment of the shoulder as previously mentioned, let the cauteries be at three points according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, since you make three of them together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, anoint the patient's back and side.
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	afterward, lift the heart that is within the titillite with your left hand.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, heat the cautery that has two nooses with which its form is made:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart until it perforates to the costeit, and bring together the figure of the cautery with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this purpose the cautery is made with one that has three nooses, so that the figures of the cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nooses follow the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three nooses:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And once adjusted above this first nerve, because of which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After place the cautery with heated coals on salt;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after making the patient rest, and let not the limbs be moved for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, little happens, then apply the fire cautery on the thick part of the joint, or several cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, thus healing the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach because it is contrary to his constitution, and the catarrh multiplies in him, and methods of treatment are accustomed but do not benefit him, then the patient should be treated on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	After this, make three cautery marks above the heel according to the size of a coin, on each cautery use a needle-cautery, and two cautery marks below the two flanks such that the shape of the cautery marks forms three angles and there is space between each other so they do not join together when putrefaction occurs.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cautery marks be so complete that they penetrate the two parts of the thigh, and let the shape of the cautery marks follow this form without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery on the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who is afraid of this cautery, prick and bleed at the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you see fit.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with all the cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we had before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver comes to pain from cold and moisture and great wind, as long as it is forced from its natural complexion due to excess.
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and if it does not profit him, then the patient must be treated on his liver.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark three cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, over the hypochondria, where the gallbladder is located.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and there should be space between each cautery the size of a thumb;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be as long as the torso, and do not press too much with your hand on the entire cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let it be burned only halfway to the heart, and let the patient lie straight on his back.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if it cannot lie on its back, let it be supine and extend its legs, and elevate its arms.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	and if you wish to burn these cauteries of the liver, be subtle and skilled in the art, and make sure you do not burn the entire heart, for you would dry up the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not come to a boil, for the veins are very delicate there, and one must be careful to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the capsule:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too severe;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the capsule, the pain is intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment reaches the membranes, it is necessary that the patient be anesthetized at its head.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then cut the vein or the abscess, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a ray of sun, as its form is:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And apply the fire cautery until the scars are arid, and continue until syphilis comes, until the eruptions are completely gone;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of sores until they are healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not fitting to use this cautery except by those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have never been corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly operate, and always it seems to me that women value it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	for the cautery of pleuresin
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make the fire cautery from roots of aristolochia, and in such manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take one root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and dry it, making it as thick and as long as you need;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and the marrow in oil, and impress with fire, and cauterize with the fire between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small fires a little descending in the part below the chin;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauterizations between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclining slightly backward;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cauterization between the buttocks, and one above the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the back below the cauterization between the shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand much, but apply it openly as in anointing.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And an ancient said that no man uses the fire cauterization in place of shaving, and heats it and places it between the ribs until it comes to that abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and when the pain is gone, as we have said for the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or fistula arises which cannot be cured.
de la mice	from the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not profit at all, then apply three methods of cautery that are all good.
