et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the grooves be just like the other two all along the forehead downward to the neck, and the others on both sides above the papers, and take care not to incise the arteries that are above the papers on both sides.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and move your hand away from the continuity of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the size of three doyles through joined.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and a bit of cloth to wipe the blood, then apply the sharp end of the spatula from both sides where it is formed.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is down to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and cauterize the entire heart that is between the two grooves until the subcutaneous tissue above the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove firmly this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert into the first cut the instrument called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is a scoop, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the blade cutting towards the buttock at the core, and the scoop blade towards the bone, and keep it in place until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	and cauterize all the vessels that descend to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to those that appear on the heart, then do the same from the middle groove to the other opening.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the limb for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then place a tent of old cotton in each fissure, and cover with moistened cloths in wine and oil and grease, and keep the abscesses from forming.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day release the bandage, and apply great plantain in hot water, then treat with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of eye pain
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When someone frequently gets acute catarrh, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and weakening of vision, and burned papers;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair itches, and when they scratch at the pain, the patients sneeze;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then know from these accidents that those materials and the catharrhe do not come forth only from many veins, and the more they are cured, so it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should instruct the patient to look behind their forehead, then make a large incision through the forehead, and another one of lesser width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And start from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let it be an incision up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then dry between the two edges of the incision and put old cotton, and line it with linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind above with moist cloths in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with excipients that promote flesh growth.
En teil maniere:	In a similar manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take 2 parts of flour of wheat, and 4 parts of colocynth, and make a plaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer this in the wounds to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the blocking of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, like grain, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or fluid-like substances like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear a stone or some other kind of thing that does not stick to the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, and it exudes any drop of violet oil or silk worm oil, then proceed with its extraction.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and cause the patient to sneeze by condisi, and stop the nose with a plug when the sneezing begins, and place in the ear pieces of cloth or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and put the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times a fistula comes about from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come about, the patient undergoes the extraction with subtle forceps, of which its form is this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it bursts with the forceps, that is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	and if not, the patient undergoes the extraction with the fine hook of small curvature;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not burst with that, make a spider's thread and insert the end of the thread or a hole in the ear firmly, and plug around the thread with soft wax so that the fistula cannot enter with the thread;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then let the treatment continue, for often it comes to force as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come to force in any way, take glue of gum and take the awls, and put in some instrument which is sharp for this purpose, and put a little cotton between;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is, and force the treatment.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	and if it does not come to force from all these things that we have said, hasten to incise the ear as one would an abscess filled with pus and decayed tissue.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the incision is that you first anesthetize the patient with the shoulder treatment, and draw out the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then place the patient's head between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or bone depends.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the incision be as wide as a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and continue the treatment until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is a grain that is embedded and inflamed, administer the extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, administer the spatule with a fine blade according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this if you think the grain is moist from ear moisture, until you have made many pieces.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with fine tongs and in suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, then the patient should use nose blowing with initial conditions, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it drains forcefully through that, that is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, take several stones according to the length of your strong and light hand, and heat them slightly on fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and place one or two of his ear stones on it. Strike from another side with another stone on the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and continue to strike the stone on the stone until the fluid runs out completely, and then it will run out completely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, take a rush, and place one of the heads in the ear, and the other head over fire until the rush is well heated;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then repeat with other rushes until the fluid runs out completely, as we have said in the case of the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large size that can be felt, apply the extraction with forceps;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the thing easiest to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and for distillations, and the cure does not help much, then you should look at the ear with the sun.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if there are no worms apparent, draw them out with fine forceps, and if they do not appear, use the wire of the form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow inside and wide outside.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the finest needle into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then proceed gradually to the entire canal;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often enough that all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, stuff the canal with cotton as I have said in the case of the stone.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in removing worms, and you will find them discussed in treatises on distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which the form is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be of thin silver or tin, below the small hole, and above the spout for distillation.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And for pressing within the distillation to the well-made instrument of tin, and if you wish take the rasp and envelop around the tip akin to cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then throw in your oil or juice, and what you wish from your medicines into the wick, and the wick be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then pour the rasp into all the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or movement of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be slightly heated on the fire as if one were distilling in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the blocking of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who has no perforations in the ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens to adults due to a wound clot or flesh grown inside the ear, and these clots sometimes do not allow them to be seen in the ear.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes the perforation is only partially blocked, and one can see through it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which is blocked and one cannot see through it, often requires careful treatment, and in such cases, you should place the ear of the patient in the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and look within:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the operation apparent, if the work has all this spatumile of which this is formed:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not damage the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the operation is on cartilage or tissue of the ear, use fine forceps, and gently scrape it until all the cartilage is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the excision is performed in the ear, take the fine razor gently and heat it a little on fire, then place it over the ear wax.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you sense the operation where the patient feels pain in the ear, gently puncture it, and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then place in the ear a tent according to the size of the puncture, and fill it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Make this for any day while the wound is healing, or take a tent and marrow in rosewater, and powder on ground glass.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary to treat the tent and move another wet tent made of rose oil and wax until the swelling is removed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding which are or involve distillation.
de la char des papieres	from the juice of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This is the herb that comes from papers of eyes when they are moist and are dried. It is necessary to spread them with tongs and forceps, and the decoction of a spathillum from its roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on the glass ground.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without scraping, cauterize with the thin lens cautery, and the cauterizer after incision moves.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often return, since nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the hailstone.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times on the eyelids come papers that appear like hail in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "hail," and it is an assembly of moisture large within the paper above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The operations are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take heed of the one who is mute on both sides, and this is a light matter to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	then cut it open wide, then brandish each part lightly, then take it with the tongs, and clamp it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot clamp it without piercing a bit the paper, then do not harm the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the cut is large, suture it up, and treat it until it heals;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not apply much force, for the ointments will restore it quickly and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	and if the shoulder is dislocated inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and expose the shoulder with tongs, and clamp and press it from both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is removed by the incision, it matters not;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the boil is cut, rinse the eye with salt water, and treat the wound with what flows from it until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that is extracted from the rags of paper bags, and this happens more to children than to adults, and greatly harms their eyes, causing catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this, they lie on their faces down, and sleep thereon, and have their papers beneath them that are moist with exinach which inflames and conceals the appearance in their eyes.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the shoulder between your fingers and feel the exinach within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is such that the patient places their head on your side;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and set up a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains outside each part, then put it on;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on both sides, so that the outside parts are gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	and make in the middle of the moisture a slit with a sharp spoon, and let it not be any wider than the incision we make in the healthy vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and open the skin thoroughly until you see the outside parts;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many positions there comes out from the wound exudate according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Draw out then entirely one piece of cloth between thy two fingers at the wound, and turn thy hand to right and left until it is dispersed;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and keep that thou dost not adder in the wound, that thou come not to all the space until the eye, that thou bleach it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exudate does not open at the beginning of the wound, so enlarge a bit the wound lightly until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then draw out as we have said, then weten with a cloth and in water, and put upon the wound, and drain of lint.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who grind grain and put it there to腐化 those remaining moistures.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is an abscess hot in the wound, treat with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When in papers grow hairs different from the natural ones, and are established, they harm the eyes, and bring about diseases such as accustomed tears, softening of the papers, and albugine, until it is a cause of destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and it is the treatment according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cautery altogether with heat, or by aqueous medicine as in the chapter on cautery, and it is done or by incision and suturing or by cantharides, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient on your healthy side, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, prick with a needle along the entire thread;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let the thread be on the edge of the paper where the hair grows from these hairs, and pull the thread up across the entire paper, and shave it with a razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut in the part beneath the paper, beneath the adjusted hairs, all the way to the sputum hole from the large hair down to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the paper, then sprinkle on the paper an amount like the leaf of juniper, as you see fit for the quantity removed from the paper which is divided for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is someone who needs it, one should use a great quantity of the paper according to how much the paper has been softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then fill the spatula up to two lines that you have marked, and begin with the large spoon until small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one be a groove near the natural hairs in the size of a root, then pour an ounce into one of the two corners of the ear, then cauterize it completely.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then缝合两个唇部用一根细羊毛线穿过针眼，然后擦去血迹，并在两条丝线上刮除多余的线头，如果你打算这样做。
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if you do not, then do not worry about it, simply leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without a stitch with drying and binding substances, for the paper remoistens suddenly from the wound and its assembling, but the stitch is moved (as the ancients say), and these are works without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if you moisten the paper with a shape that is as large as the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, sew it on three sides according to the form which is described:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply those that surpass the small forces evenly according to the form which is given here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the strength to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, take an needle with one thread, and sew through the shape;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and pull out one thread from the large wick, and the second thread from the small one, and join the two threads evenly;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above where you have marked, as we have recounted, then join the two edges of the wound by suturing, and treat until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with a plaster and similar soothing ointment;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes the hair of the paper is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you must use what we have said about the incision:
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitch on one side and the other is more artificialized.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment for canine teeth is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and you must convert the paper and cut it inside according to what I have said, and then make two canine teeth by art, and two ligaments also long as the paper and as wide as the spacing is.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and hold the threads at the head of the part where you have the fibers.
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble the one and the other delicately on what surmounts from the paper of the oil, and hold the two canine teeth from the two parts firmly.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it thus for some days, and the skin which is constrained will die, wither, and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, and the wound has strength, then treat it until it heals.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is healed, and the paper is lifted, the hairs will not grow anymore.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the form of the two cauterizations that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the operation is such that you take a sharp needle, and thread through it thin and subtle.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then join the heads and tie both subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the chase another thin silk thread briefly, and tie the heads of the threads together;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then place the patient's head on your side;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and keep away from the sun so that the work be clear, for it is a delicate and small operation. Then place the needle throughout the chase at the root of the added hair, and pierce the paper quickly as you pull it over the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then extract the hair until it reaches the chase, and place that hair in the chase if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then draw out your hand when the hairs have grown outside completely through the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the paper is treated and the hairs do not come through with it, draw out the paper from around all the threads that you have ordered, until the paper comes through completely above and you see it with the eye's sight;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then draw out the paper and the threads, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 days or 3, until the hair grows in its place and flesh appears above.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is small, accompany it with a long natural hair, and lift it along with that one or leave it, until it stretches, then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the putrefaction of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this illness which is called "aleacrait" or corruption comes to the eye, there are two ways of it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or surgery, or the fire cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut the seam, and separate the edges of it, and put within sutures of linen, and bind it tightly until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not fitting that you use in the treatment of such things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but use things that soften, such as fenugreek.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and let the application of water or vinegar and linseed that have been cooked, and unguents melted in any oil, be applied, and wrap it in a cloth.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the dressing of your wound is that you take care that it does not heal improperly according to the form it had before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have said must be applied such that the illness does not return according to the form it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the method of the work is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and sew into the flesh, and make the thread pierce from left to right so that the threads pass through two heads of the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then the flesh is drawn above to all the needle, and the skin to the broad surface.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper figure returns as it should, that is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	and if not, take the scissors and place them in the裂口，然后转动纸张，在纸内侧形成两个裂口；
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the heads of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision you have made, and make angles such that when they are assembled, the shape is as in the shape of a letter which has an "I" or "griesche".
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that your fingers are able to grasp from beneath, then join the two severed parts, and stitch them with a linen thread.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the treatment of what we have said regarding softening medicines and bandages until he is cured.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a wound or suture or fire cautery, it is necessary that you make a full incision under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two flaps of a dressing, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the masters prepare means of all their power to make the body return to its natural form.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what needs to be done and instruments in various preparations.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this seam happens to men in such a manner that the paper above is hardened with the white of an egg and cannot move nor perform its natural works, then you must therefore put the point of a razor beneath the paper and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and remove with forceps, until you take out what is attached to the thin membrane, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer from the thin membrane being too sharp and blistering the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and make your incision, which you burn together gently, so that the paper returns according to its natural form.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and the entire assembly is healthy, and do this not once in the eye that is sore and salty, and rinse it with sweet water, and from anger.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put over the eye moistened wool from an egg.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use a colander and dark things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and resembles hard syphilis, and another which is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture, such that when touched with iron and treated with tweezers, it cannot be removed.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both resemble starting from the large lid and gradually increasing a little by little until they cover the entire field of vision and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incising is such that the patient places their head on your lap, then open their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and hold the paper with your hand, then place the nail against the forceps of small size, and extend it above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert the hair of a horse, or a cow, or a bull, and a strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle slightly and stitch through the nail, piercing it completely with the needle. Hold the nail steady above and burn along the side of the nail that has the groove and the thread to the hair until reaching the root, then cut off the remaining part with fine forceps and small strength, leaving the natural skin or horn at the root, so that the body does not weep tears through this incision as it is accustomed to doing.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail grows on its own, and on the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then the scorching affects all the spatumile_soup of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And ensure that the spatumile does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the prunelle remains intact;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour some burned salt into the eye, and from a necklet made of litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with what is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot pierce it with a needle, and the pins cannot enter it, often this resemblance of a nail is treated with medicines.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it copulate, work the eye of the patient gently with a sharp but light spatule according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And gently scrape the nail upwards, and if you see that it thins at all and the root presses on it, distill from your mouth into the eye of the mixture made of litharge and red colchicum and salt, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then resume the other operation according to this same method until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, such as an abscess, then let it alone, and first treat the warm abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh around the eyelid is harmful to the eye by great injury, suspend it with a needle, and copulate one part and not too much, so that no tears arise.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill colriere rouge into the eye, which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises around the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Some people's eyes are born with a scar red, and it covers the pupil and is held on papers and turned to decay, seeming like a water-lily rose.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the procedure is that the patient places their head on your shoulder, then closes their eyes, and you draw all that scar tissue with suitable needles to this place, and hold it in place with force.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then remove the first scar, and continue cutting down to the skin until the end, and be sure not to injure the eye in the procedure.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and the incision for the spot (or speck) should be made as we have said in the incision of the nail and with small force by which one removes the scab, as the form after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with brimstone or you may distill red cologne or similar corrosive medicines, and place over the eye a swab of egg white to keep it secure from an abscess.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if nothing remains, and the stone surmounts it, and you fear an abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with things that alleviate a hot abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do with the arrows inserted in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But always it must be that you moderate the treatment of each weak eye according to its natural course.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental way, in the work with iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If the veins around the eyes are red and cover the eye, they allow the work to be seen and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	Therefore, for the first thing you look to see if the eye, in which bel is situated, is out of place, and there is no other disease besides the bel;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then adjust it in such a manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to place their head on your side, then suspend those veins at every ounce according to your wisdom, and let the ounces be subtle and doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two ounces by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then, when one has to make those veins subtle and wipe the blood an hour after another, until you see remove those veins from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and keep from injuring the eye with the points of the speatmiles, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you do not harm only those veins.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, distill green and red bile into the eye to corrupt what remains of the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not have the power to collect all of this in that hour, apply a plaster to the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and you are assured of the warm abscess, then resume according to this method which is before mentioned until it is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	and these are the forms of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	They call such things "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you cure it with cautery and medicine of burning water as I have said before, and it is not yet healed, indeed there will be in what you cut over the abscess, sore or place where it must die, and draw out all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then remove all the instrument of which this is the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron sharp as a saw, and pointed like a rasp as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place on the head of the rotten bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little so that you know that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this once, then restore the head with medicinal desiccants.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the joints are set and flesh begins to grow, and the core of the bone is set, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not swell again and is not at all abscessed, and no bad accident happens, know that it is healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if not, there is no other means than to bring the fistula back to the perforation of the neck according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone the second time with iron and with cold medicines, and when it has been uncovered, take the saw according to this form, and let the iron head of the saw have three angles, and the blade be thin down to the teeth as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone beside the tear, and move your hand away from the eye slightly, then turn the saw entirely until it pierces the bone, and let the patient feel it through what comes from it if you keep your hand near your nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the bone with dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the bones, the matter will go to your nose;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter matter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes open completely, and there is no obstruction or diminishment, you must tie the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the healthy one, then apply suction cups or plaster without injuring to draw out the fluid, then place on the eye a salve made of acacia and aloes and incense and sarcocolla, and then apply bandages and cloths around it.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the method of cloths is that you take soft cloths, and double each one into four layers, then place them one on top of the other according to the quantity the eyes need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then draw it out from above with a hard bandage, and restart the cups to suck without piercing.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cups and let the eye remain held steady day and night, and if the ligaments soften, you must then draw it out much.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the ligature after day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good.
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the plaster and bandages and the ligature and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	for the tearing of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come in the retinal tissue, then open and come forth through the papers as if from resin grains, and is fearful to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it cover, the operations are such that you insert a needle from below the part up to that above, then insert another needle or have a double thread from the eye of the needle;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and make it pierce, and leave the first needle in place according to the disposition;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then withdraw the thread and tie a part of the uve around it, and hold it tightly, then remove the needle and place wetted wool from an egg yolk on the eye.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread is tied around the uve, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound heals.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and sometimes the wound is compressed by the cloth at each part of a circular piece, until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes appear swollen, puncture them with a fine needle that comes from the depth of the eye, and drain the moist, whitish fluid, and let them recover soon.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then extract it until it heals.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease called "alcunnati" is not caused by water that gathers in the eye, resembling descending fluid, and it is not actual water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on the prepared chair and upright, then hold the head with your hands from both sides, and move the jaw until you see the water rise to above your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then it should be pierced, and not descended and let the light out, and show the patient the things as he is accustomed to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend out, know that it is acute, and if the descensions of the bowe are not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	seat the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make a cut on the corneal membrane just along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the crown, so that the bowe comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it has come out, instill into the eye warm acrid liquid mixed with honey, or boiled acrid liquid and honey, then continue to treat with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have experienced the appearances of fevers in the division, and what needs to be pierced;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if during work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you place the patient between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and tie the healthy eye tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the cloth soaked in oil in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if the eyes are on the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are on the right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then place the tip of the instrument along the edge of the cornea by the thickness of a hair in that part beneath the minor lacrimal gland, then push the instrument, which is called "almagda," virtuously, and twist your hand until it pierces into the pulp of the eye, and feel that almagda enters the hollow part.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and the size of the almagda should be precisely that of the space from the pupil to the end of the iris.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the cornea of the eye.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone through that membrane due to the clarity of the cornea, and can place the instrument there or where the pain is, then press it out along one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the liquid flows out now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting a little, and if the fluid rises again by the second way, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and does not rise, extract slightly with a gentle turn of your hand little by little.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put a bit of the gemstone thread in water, and remove the eye from it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place something to plug the eye, such as a moistened piece of wool in rose oil and abundant egg, and secure it with healthy eye tissue.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, we place on with a cloth soaked in abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it hardens to the extent that it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are people whose eyes are too hard, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which its form is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it a fine incision, then extract slightly with a gemstone, as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and for the completion of the work, arrange for the patient to sleep on his back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be subject to all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his position until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then release him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not fitting that you do this during the hour of treatment or after incision now, but you must anesthetize him, because the fluid rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if abscesses appear, you should release the eye before the seventh day, and apply the treatment that alleviates the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is pacified, release the eye and place on its face a cover to protect any day, and let it be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then leave the house little by little, and adapt to its condition;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no decoctions should be given in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almagda pears, which they applied with water, but altogether I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the signs of the forms of almagda, because he who does not know them will be deceived;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and may they be properly of arsenic:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of aus be of this same subtlety, and the last in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there arise or do not arise new sores of various kinds, some of which seem like scorpions' bites.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such sores and he has a sore with a deep color from a burn, and if the sore is filled with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In the case of these sores that are filled and not deepened, you must place the patient's sore part in your hands against the sun.
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and cast the pinch of powder to those sores, and draw them out;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	put hold of that which you can sustain at the subtle sharp edge on one side, as long as you know that that sore is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains anything that you cannot hold, open it with all the subtle instruments gently, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if without surmounting it, or abscess covered, apply the aid as it should.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the pus is drained and all the sores are removed, then apply or sprinkle ash or dry and sharp vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the work is done and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh grown on the bone above, to which the instruments cannot come to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then you must insert a bit of thick linen thread, and tie it with our hands, leaving a little space between each knot.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and place the patient's head under the thread so that it is comfortable, and pull gently until the thread comes out through the neck into the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times children do this at school, and it is a light matter for those who know how to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes by the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes by the mouth with the other hand, and feel them one after another where we are or fit.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	do this until you know that the nose has spoiled that part of the flesh, then pull the thread, wipe the blood, soften the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back again as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put a piece of linen over the nose for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medications, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for cleansing the head, to which one administers drops of oils and medicines or urine:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be made of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a wick, and leads to;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you want to see, make a wick closed, and let the instrument be full for cleansing the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have the handle at the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times, a disease called "telul" arises at the head from urine, grows and becomes large, so that it can be seen when examined.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and because of this, you must cool it at the beginning, and let the bone completely dry, then place a fire cautery or burning medicine over it;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay cooling it until it is large, then watch to see if it is hard, pale in color, and lacking sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if it does not touch with iron at all, for this is an embedded abscess, for when it is cooled even once, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is due to a soot touchment, not pale in color, and you can completely cool it, then empty the patient and cool it with things drying and constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilages in the work, it profits little, for in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, when this occurs to anyone, see if the wound is fresh throughout its bleeding;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then adjust the two edges with suturing, and continue to treat until it is healed;
