et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary to cauterize all parts of their roots until they heal, then adjust the two edges with suturing, and bind them, and sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood, and powdered incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place over the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another healing plaster, and leave it until it scabs on its own, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of suturing is that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have told you before.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In the lips, an abscess hardens, resembling grains of wheat, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn the lips, incise along each fold, and take it with forceps and divide it into each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the ligature after the incision with the vitreous stone, until the blood is stanched;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then take the ileasis leaf, and treat the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	many times a carious tooth arises on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	then you must hold it with the tongs, and pull it to its root, and let the tooth or blood run out.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply vitriol powder, or other drying and收敛性粉末，于伤口上。
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the tooth returns after incision, and this happens many times, then pull it a second time, and cauterize it:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	and if it does not return after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments to use.
des sordens	of sorts
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes there are gathered at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth become black, yellowish, and worm-eaten, as corruption comes to the gums, and the teeth smell foul.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	and it is necessary that you seat the patient between your hands, and his head in your lap, and inspect the teeth or scabs that are visible, until there remains nothing.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus treat the blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other stains until they are removed.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is at the first reason, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, restart from the second day and the third, until you have done it all;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that teeth require various forms of instruments to be treated, according to what the operation demonstrates, for the raspers used on exposed teeth have other shapes than those used between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay the treatment as long as you can, for it should not be done immediately.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because this is a very high substance such that one cannot have any excuse for not cutting it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to extraction, it must be certain which tooth aches.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain afflicts the patient, and he believes it is from Saint Dent; and causes a good tooth to be pulled.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and in any case, the pain does not cease from this until the bad tooth is extracted, for we have already often done this to these saints.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary to cauterize around the tooth with a strong spatillum to protect the gum from all sides.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then pull it out with your tweezers or fine forceps at the first twitch and twitch, until it is well loosened, then firmly set the forceps.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's shoulder be on thy holy lap between thy knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After drawing the tooth rightly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and insert it gently from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	and if the wound is pierced and ragged, it must be filled with cloths, lint, or the like;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you clamp it gently with forceps, do not break it in clamping;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it must be deeply cut between the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it and leave a part behind, as this will cause the patient greater pain than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	and take care that you do not do so as the ignorant surgeon does, who, through their haste and boldness, break the bone sometimes, and do not provide them with what we have recounted;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but they bring about sometimes through the incision of that great illness due to the roots remaining, or to the decay that they break, as we have often willed.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash the area with wine or ale and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if the bleeding continues, which often happens, apply the area with ground vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments for extracting teeth should be with long points and large handles, so that they do not bend when you are drawing the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have thick handles so that they do not bend when extracting, and let them be made of well-forged iron, and let them have teeth to hold tightly.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	and when the root remains during drawing, it must be that you place wetted cloth in butter on the area for one or two days until the flesh is softened, then remove the pliers called "algefri" with which the head seems to be grasped like a cup.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and may also be made inside like a file and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these tongs, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And it should be hollow and large so that it does not break, and if the root passes through it, that is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms are given hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need to use an instrument that has two prongs, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front according to the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument that seems like large tongs, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument not be breakable, and know that most dental instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not described;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the master arrows find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the disease show them, for there are diseases where the old ones did not teach any instruments because of the diversity of bones, or they rot, so they seek the appropriate instruments, as I have said, and help with gestures, of which the form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-designed to hold the bone, so it does not escape but can be held and removed.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the head of the bone with suitable medicine, and if there is corruption in the bone and it is small, remove it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not at all according to its natural course, and the form is ugly, especially in maiden women, you must know whether the tooth has grown after its place and is not in the right position, and cannot be corrected or smoothed.
adonques lou raie;	then use the point.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is placed with the tooth, take this instrument of which the form is described, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And file the teeth little by little in your hand for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that they can be smoothed, then smooth them with a piece of fine sandpaper as described.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file with which we make needles.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and file the tooth little by little with my hands gently, so that it does not move until it heals;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the plain in the end for any razor, and if the edges are too sharp and it blackens the tongue, then file the harshness until it is equal, so that it does not blacken the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth chatter
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth decay, or through impact or falling, and the patient cannot grasp what they eat without dropping it, and you have treated them with medicine that constricts, yet this is not effective;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then you must restrain them with a gold thread, for the silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you wish to treat the teeth, take the thread and the needle double between two healthy teeth, then place the heads between the affected teeth, whether there is one or more, as long as you can clearly reach the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then continue the bandaging until you reach the part where you started, and withdraw your hand gently and steadily, ensuring it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and tie your thread at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	then cut the heads of the thread with tweezers, and join them, and rethread them between the healthy tooth, and place them such that they do not choke the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then let it remain so tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, you must tighten it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it remains and serves so for its entire duration, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment of the two healthy teeth, as well as the two molar teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, you place it back in its place, frequently as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let no one who is not wise and suffers do it in any case. And once, the form of a tooth of a bovine bone was made, and this tooth was placed in the place where the tooth is missing, and it was tightened as we have said, and remained and served for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover up the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this comes from the tongue or natural causes, that one is born thus.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a healed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the operations are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and place his head on your lap, and tie his tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve ligament wide open, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or a knot, and it is due to a sudden wound, then use a lancet and cut that ligament wide.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be sure that the cut is not too deep, for the artery is beneath it.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done, lift the shoulder from the basin of rose water and almond, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and let the patient apply it every night, so that the swelling cannot subside.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, place quickened vitriol over the swelling.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the bleeding continues, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	and continue to treat until they are healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it is of a rusted color or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a sore.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining to blackworm, and there is moisture, he should give the ounce, and make a small hole with a lancet, and deliver from both sides;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the wound turns against your work, he should place vitriol powder until it is effused, then return to your work as long as you drain all pus;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the dressing of flax and silk, and treat other wounds until they are healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes blisters appear in the throat called "godath," and they are properly known as two almonds. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is abscesses hard with small sensation and flesh colored, do not let them touch with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if they are red and the root is swollen, do not let them be touched with iron at all, nor for the discharge of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let them be until they are dead, and then you shall cut them out, or they would break on their own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if they are white in color and the root is fine, prepare the instrument to cauterize, but first see if the abscess has cooled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then seat the patient in front of the sun, and their head be towards you, and let them close their mouth and have the servant hold their head between their hands, pressing the tongue underneath the entire instrument, which is its form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and may it be of fine silver or tin as thin as knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	And press the tongue with all this instrument, and if you see the abscess, take an ounce and prick it like an almond, and draw out more than you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and draw out nothing from the threads with it, then cover the instrument, of which its form seems like force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and always the head is curved, and one against the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, use tongs, of which the form is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And may it be sharp on one side, and on the other called;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner, and after incising, gargle the patient with hot sharp water, or with hot and easy water, and if there is a flow of blood, gargle the patient with water, or with cooked pomegranate peelings, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is expelled.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then continue the treatment until he is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and if other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, then cut them in the same manner as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had appeared in her throat, namely the small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had almost completely closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not expire due to the constricted passage which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained in such a condition for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had to be lanced through both openings of the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened quickly, and pierced one inch, then pulled out the needle, and drew out a large portion of blood;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then pierced the other side at another hole in the nose, and opened his mouth and pressed his tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after piercing the inch into these abscesses, and drained a part of them, and only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the passage of the throat was opened for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to lance this abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses repeatedly formed again, and filled the wound that I had emptied, until it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I set it and cauterized inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	then the swelling ceased to grow.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left those parts, and let God decide what would happen to them thereafter.
de l’uve	from the eye socket
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When rheumatism affects the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are healed and are fine, then it is necessary that you lance them.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round gathered and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and if it is bloody or of reddish color or black, then it is necessary that you incise it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it in the manner I have said, of its hardness and length, you should place the patient facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the oncine into the eye, and draw it out, and lance with the second instrument as I said in the incision of the almond.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not apply force that is beyond the natural limit.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	and if you apply more force, you may harm the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, you must use an instrument for the cautery to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient place their head on your lap, and then press their tongue with the instrument we have mentioned or the fire cautery, using a sharp tool, so that it is not too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and apply the edge of this instrument, whose form is as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let there be one hair or where one places the medicine, as with the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument above all the medicine on the eye;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth over the medicine, without descending to the throat, and the cloth.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the eye, for half an hour, until you see it nerveless and the bites of the medicine are alleviated.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in the tube above, until the cotton is saturated on the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterizations are perfect, then let it dry, and fall after four days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to re-start the cauterization for the medicine, do so, and after the cauterization, wipe it around the wound with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be rinsed with cold water, and be washed with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision or cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is washed with fumigation in this manner, take calamus, yarrow, origanum, rue, chamomile, and valerian, and gather all of these or any of them in one pot, and put asbestos in it, and boil it.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the poultice should be well mixed with strong earth, and within the pot have the instrument cover according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And may be of silver or lead, and let one of the heads be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is numbed;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the rekindling often, until the eye dries, and keep that you do not perform this at the beginning of the onset of the hot abscess, for many things happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not perform this when the hot abscess is subsiding.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put a chicken feather inside it, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the fear of an egg does not allow vapor to weigh down the mouth, and this is a good treatment overall for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it is applied to the throat, bone or spiny fish, or any other thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so you must treat what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not become clear and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit as if the meat were cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance, if the thing is expelled by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and ties it to the sponge with a thread, and then swallows it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, it will expand, and then you will draw out the force.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come to force as we have said, take the probing instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be inserted at the throat such that it can enter more easily into the throat, and keep the head lifted upwards.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful that you do not touch the epiglottis, for if you do, it may close and block the airway, nor should you push the bone in.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and when moved, it is fitting for the patient to stop using the instrument, because it has been moved or the thing is raw.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if it has been drawn back, or he pulls it out forcefully with the entire instrument equally.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Never is the sinew medicated, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not profit at all, then look at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, and press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the pus, draw it out with a very small lancet, or with fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, take a live cane, insert it into the throat of the patient, then blow or shake the cane with hot air, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is thirsty all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, pour it into the mouth, and let it go down, and move it often with his hand.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood feels cold, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with arsenic sulfide using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the uvea.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall without difficulty.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are burning charcoal, and place the head of the patient covered with a perforated lid in the middle, and through those holes place the heads of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then throw in the fumigating substance, and the patient put the head of the cane in their mouth, and close the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape but goes to the blood;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the pus will now flow out, and if it does not flow, resume the fumigation multiple times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient feels thirst, eats salty and stale food, and does not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is necessary for her to be forced out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the pus is such that when one can see it, it resembles curved forceps meant to enter the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles a surgeon's claw, and it has a rough surface like that of a file, such that once it touches something, it cannot be released.
et vez ci la forme:	and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to what memory brings after in this book, and they differ in puncture and incision;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways, of which one is in its own appearance and of what it holds, being moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the sores or where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the solid part, and abscesses of flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if for abscesses one should not pierce, until the boil is dead according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if for such cases one should pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are deep in joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, and one lets them remain until they are rotten within, by chance the ligaments and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the abscess is close to the main member, and if you delay the puncture until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or it is close to the foundation, if you puncture it thus when it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not fitting that you puncture an abscess that is firm before digestion is completed, even if it is close to the foundation, so that it does not rot completely and becomes extended within, and may become a fistula;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a great while.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the time of puncturing the abscess when it is ripe according to completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the softening and ripening of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you must place the perforation or more dependent part of the abscess, and where it opens and moves;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or at joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equal where there is no pleura.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the living flesh, it is better to let the perforation remain until digestion is completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you perforate before it, the venom of the abscess will spread along the body, and be filled with much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance harden the edges and the deeper parts of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is perforated according to the size of the body, as the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	and you must apply to small abscesses, small punctures;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large wounds, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if such large abscesses require making a hole in the heart, and applying;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	and when it has become as soft as wool, and is softened, then you must do so as one does for boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such ones that are split into three angles, and if there are such ones that one applies salve to like the leaf of laurel, as for abscesses of the insane.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such ones where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar applications.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, as with a superficial abscess sore, it must be pierced completely.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And it must be done when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, if you pierce it, do not draw all the pus at once in that hour, but draw a part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then dress the abscess until the next day, then draw no more pus again.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times gradually, until all the pus has drained out.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	the same is done if the patient has weak constitution, or is a woman pregnant, or small children, or old and infirm.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because the patient trembles several times with the discharge of the pus, that by chance kills the patient, and you will not know this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and look to see if the wound from the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a clean incision, apply tents of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many perforations, then you must apply a tent in each so that they come together;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have incised part of the skin over the abscess and closed it with a stitch, then you must fill it with old cotton or shreds of dry linen cloth, and bind it until the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the treatment with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is an evacuation of blood in your work, you apply cold water and ease the pain, and cover with soft linen, and place over the area where the blood flows repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding continues, apply a government and treatment, and the powders that I have said in my hand book, and if it is or tends to be cold, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, you must place wet cloths and woolen drapes soaked in wine and hot oil on them.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in summer, and the wound is fleshly, you must place wet cloths in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, for three days, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then drain the abscess, clean it, and treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or I have told you how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or come from the head small abscesses, and they are like those in fabrics, as with the fibers of a flax plant, and there are many that resemble them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are fat ones and such, which have moisture as well as boils;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and there are such ones that are hard and stony to the knife, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause harm.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the flank are such that you test with any instrument called "intromissory," from which the form follows, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, he lets it drain from above downward.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, burn it without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, because it will reaccumulate if nothing is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, with water and thread, and dress the wound, leaving it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and let those who have been delayed overnight continue.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then continue with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not delay overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dress the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds onto fat, then apply the compress according to this form, of long duration.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and pourge your veins, and scorch it from all sides, and apply all your treatment to draw the poison where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery gives you contrary results, do as I said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and treat as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut for the stony abscess and its moisture is lighter, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if in any of these abscesses or head injuries there is no moisture, and these are the abscesses that I treated or head injury of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess as hard as a dull stone, rough and white, and could not be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if any had been made of it, it would have also been as well injured as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or affecting the head, it must be that the opening remain always at the lowest part of the head, so as to allow the bowels to escape.
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat the wounds as they should.
des scrophules	of gland swellings
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times such abscesses occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in angles, and sometimes appear elsewhere on the body, they are hard, and are joined together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its groove, just as the knot and abscess of the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the similarities of these scrofula are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in which you see good placement upon touch, and resembles the color of the body, mute in each part and not inverted near the neck nor near the artery nor the vein, and is not deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	then you should cut it open from above, and scorch each part, and place the two lips of the wound with the stitches, if you have need to do so, just as we have said for abscesses of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and draw a little bit by little bit, and be sure that you do not hit the nerve nor the vein, and neither the spatumileagus nor the trenchers, that your hand does not escape, and do not go too far, so as not to hit what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you hit the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to continue, apply vitriol powder or any other powders that staunch blood, and compress the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is relieved, and the wound softens and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is staunched, return to your work until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then you should examine if there are any small scrofulous swellings left, and cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofulous swelling, it is not advisable to cut that swelling at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and proceed to the treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and suture them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cut the root of it, and draw out the force, and suture it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulous swellings due to excess, puncture them where they appear to drain.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and puncture them in the same way as previously mentioned, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then apply the ointment cure until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrophula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke and wrote about the surgery of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with scrophula, it is necessary to incise the slit in the throat which is called "epiglote";
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and do not seek help from them, for their veins and the nearby parts of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the tonsil, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It must therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglote, be cut over three or four small cuts across, between the two circles or by the size of the cut through the skin, and not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if the veins are suitable for cutting the epiglote so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in that area.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it must be stretched from the entire length of the throat to the tip, then cut the skin until it reaches the muscle.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and cut the blood vessels if you see any, then sew up the skin as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein from the elbow which jumps out because the bone is broken, and by the loss of voice due to fault.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a day.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed since there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart, and stitch it well without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that produce flesh, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis said that this should not be done until the throat is completely numb, and the patient is judged to be dying, and then proceed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then treat the epiglottis for those who cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and because of this, the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the mischief of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. Then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it until it is healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took the knife, and stabbed it into her throat, and cut part of the veins there.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood issuing from it. I knew that she had not pierced a vein nor any great artery, but the blood was coming from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened there, dressed the wound, and treated it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and there was no change in the lady's voice, and she returned to her usual state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for I say that in the operation of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "goiter," and it is a large abscess in the color of a liver, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two methods:
naturez, et accidens;	nature, and accident;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or naturally there is no mechanism.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is according to two methods, of which one resembles a fatty lump, and the other method resembles an abscess that comes from within the artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and if there is fear, it should not be operated on except in what is small, and the proof and search are made of all that interferes:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as we find fat, and cannot be drawn to any vein, pinch it, as one pinches fat, and draw it with its skin, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well around it, and treat it as it should be treated, until it is completely healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many methods for dealing with fats exist, of which I will describe all the similarities.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now it is necessary for me to say all the difference that exists between fat and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that heat and fever arise until the boiling is passed and the putrefaction is completed.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new one having no heat, fever, or pain, and containing pus, which is its own secretion and according to the color of the body, and begins like a jelly, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they vary according to their appearance, or grease, or moisture, and not much in color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It must be, when you come to the treatment of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "intermissive," according to what its form will come or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring into abscesses for us is that you prick more moist parts of the lump you find in the abscess, and turn your needle little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core. Then it must be according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the interposer, and take care that it not jump.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture flows out, regardless of its color, treat it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the interposer no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then incise it in a cross shape, and remove it with forceps, and gently cauterize each part. Take care where it lies and treat the surrounding tissue with hot oil to ensure it heals properly.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot treat it properly, remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will cause us trouble many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if one remains a little, and the wound grieves, fill the wound with certain corrosive powders moistened, hold the wound, and apply hot abscess-sothing things until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, suture the two edges of the wound, and treat it with what nourishes flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the pulsing vein is contrary or another that requires haste, apply the juice of ground vitriol, and let it remain for two or three days, until the wound rots, and rest the boiling of the blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to the copper that has remained from new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the intervening instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	great, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three square ones which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are of three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	great, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews ligatures, and they are made of yellow brass or iron or silver, and it is said that those that are yellow are more effective for surrounding the cords of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the oncin are like wool in resemblance, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if oncin have two corbeures of three ways also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if oncin have three corbeures, and are also of three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if oncin have two corbeures, and oncin with only one corbeure, and are of three ways;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these for which one makes them is sharp, and among such one cuts with force only from one side, by which one sears the nostrils, because one does not cut the vein nor the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these inserters are the wicks placed in the thumbs, so that the patient does not perceive them during the incision of abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one uses force only in flabby areas, such as legs, arms, mammary glands, and angles, and in similar places.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another instrument is made small, resembling the shells of nuts, according to this form, with which one stops the bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed once in its place where it heals by degrees from the veins, and in the arteries, and once more according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, to the point where they resemble women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen. Whoever needs to treat them should do so according to this form from line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then burn the fat, and fill the wound with flesh-inducing medicine. Then suture the two edges of the wound together and treat it until it heals.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags down and becomes soft due to its size, as happens in women, cut it open at two ribs above, using similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	of which one should be held to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contain the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cauterize the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment until he is cured;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not cured, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not wish to rest, or due to the bleeding, it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton soaked in a腐蚀性药膏;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until the patient drinks the remedy and the fat are removed, then treat the wound until he is cured.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of arrow wounds
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from arrow wounds are similar to hard scrofula glands, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b. to the line g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowe that is in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment appropriate for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula glands, incise it as we have said for incisions in scrofula, and if the wound contains bowe, apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin above is sewn up, there often arise abscesses; likewise, it happens with an inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, let the abscesses remain long to form.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your hands, feel the constriction;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is due to the vein, let it be relieved by evident swelling;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to treat this abscess, especially when it is near the armpits and angles and under the arm and many other parts, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid the iron cure, and he who is in pain should also avoid it, and in that which is swollen from an artery, cut through the skin above the long hair;
