puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then cut the incision at the inch marks, and cleanly separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle and pierce it until the other side, and hold the artery with a doubled thread at two ends, as I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then pull the intervening limb between the two threads until the fluid comes out, and then release the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment that follows, until the ligaments heal;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with ointment appropriate for this, until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is as large as the vein, it must be that you draw out as much of the abscess as you can from the entire area, then insert the needle under the skin you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and use a double thread, so that you pull from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then bind the abscess as I have told you, or with a ligament from one part to the shoulder.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is strong enough, then insert another needle through the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four knots.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then incise the abscess until the excess flows out, then incise the kidney and leave what is tied.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place on the wound a cloth soaked in wine and oil, then give him treatments and applications until he is cured.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come to the artery and vein, abscesses of the nerves when they are injured, or through too great labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in joints and bones, and in all places where there are joints, and it is the cause of abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions with pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one extracts it forcefully, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely due to the body, but beneath the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and must move well from all sides, and not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and that which is in joints should not be treated with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance it might contract;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and that which is on the head or forehead, open the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, take it with forceps, and treat it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a needle, and cauterize it, then extract it and suture the wound, and continue to treat until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and is a disease called "fungus" by its similarity to mushrooms, and the head is small, and the shoulder large;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are both small and very large;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a home which had two or more bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were slightly split, and within corroded thus with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them and found in one eighteen ounces weighing, and in the other six ounces. The work in incision is such that you should examine if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and has fine roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if you cut them with the spoon broad, and let the cautery on fire be in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in the tailor often comes too great hemorrhages, and if he dies, then you must hasten to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision with the iron, then take a well-madeawl thread, and place it on the artery as we have said, and let it hang for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then secure it, and do not cease to hold the awl thread until it grasps the artery, and continue to monitor the work;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, do not fear to grasp them immediately for the abdomen, but you may well grasp half of them, then cauterize so that they do not return;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and ensure you do not touch the nipple which is of fleeing color and of poor sensation and has regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess embedded, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is hot
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the bubo comes from a fire cautery or a cut by a needle, and is on the abdomen and there are some in the groins, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as was mentioned before, or from wind.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the rupture of the bowel and the discharge of the bubo, then its color resembles that of an abscess, similar to the body's color, and it is a slight thing with little pain, and shows various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more varied. When pressed at its roots, it rises and then returns. Sometimes it swells significantly upon entering the bath and due to great strain.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and clearly shows when you press it with your hand; it does not constrain much.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is for blood, open by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and puncture according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is for windiness, it is sore to the touch, and the work is that you look whether the appearance is due to blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You must let the treatment continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bladder, you must instruct the patient to stretch his abdomen, and be extended entirely straight, then draw the belt around the entire waist;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to lie very still in your hands, then go around the limb where you have drawn the belt completely around the entire circumference, then place half of the abscess above at the level of the great inch;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it tightly with a strong thread or a firm cord of strong silk, and let it be tied firmly in place.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work the midpoint of the abscess extended over the thread, and place your index finger inside, and hold the intestine steady.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught on the thread, release it, and place the intestine at the rear of the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the boil, take it with forceps, and drain the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery makes it difficult, or the vein, go gently inside, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through, and place the needles where you made the puncture.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then extract the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the wound until it rots, and cut out the dead flesh.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you let it come when it is subtle and rotten, then treat the wound as needed, and cut out the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as needed, and close the wound with sutures.
dou chancre	of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken of the symptoms of chancre and how one should treat it with medicines, and how one must avoid treating it with iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and we say that the chancre occurs in the groin, and great caution is needed in its treatment. The ancients said that when a chancre can be scraped away, like one found on the sameles or in the thigh, and similar areas, it should be entirely removed when it is in the early stages.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, it does not suit you to approach it, for I have never cured any of them.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one has ever cured any of them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the procedures, when it is set or can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the patient once of black bile;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him healthy if he has evident fullness, then prepare the patient well set so that the work can be done.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then throw out the warts or scabs, and the hair from all parts, and remove it from all parts leaving nothing behind.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and hold the limb well in your hand or with some object, and if the bleeding contradicts the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stanched.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already described the symptoms of dropsy, and how the gathering of the fluid is made, and the signs for each symptom, and the treatment with medicines, and that which is treated with a iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only swollen.
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not apply iron in these two symptoms:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	this is to know, otitis and hyperpyrexia, because it is a deadly thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	therefore when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not help, then see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as an attack of wind or similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if you do not apply iron, because there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient is of strong vitality, and he has no other illness except dropsy alone, and he is neither too weak nor too old, then proceed in this manner to treat:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lay the patient on his side on your hands, and the attendants press the abdomen by directing water to the lowest part of the sore, then take the thorn spatillum according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	With a point, and in any case should not be inserted so deep that it could come as far as the intestines when one drives it in, and he cannot bend it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then see if the hydrocele is directed towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you incise upwards from the groove III down along the blade of the knife;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the hydrocele is due to the disease of the liver, let your incision be on the left side of the groove III down.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to the spleen, let it be on the right side, and it is not appropriate that the patient lies on the incision so that the excess fluids do not flow to that weak side.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	pierce all the skin with the instrument, and cut out, and lift your hand from all the spatumile between the skin and the subcutaneous tissue as in cauterizing to the quantity of a nail or about that.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	pierce the subcutaneous tissue until the spatumile comes to its proper place, and this is the seat of the fluid, then draw out, and remove this instrument whose form it has.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a thin silver needle, made of fine or light metal, and has on the part below the small puncture.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three punctures;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other part, and one on the other;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head of the shoulder is cut like a quill, and this is the form of the incision that writers cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	above the head is the alemele, so that when the instruments come to the edge, they now lie above the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	draw out then the half or the third part, for if you draw out more than is appropriate in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the release of his spirit from the weapon, or he may fall senseless, or he comes near to death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but draw out according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then draw the instrument and hold the fluid, and it is now held to prevent the perforation which is on the syphax, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner.
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then repeat the procedure on the other side, if you see the patient suffering, and draw a small quantity of fluid.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this every day, and be careful not to follow it too much so as to leave any significant amount of fluid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much fluid, let the wound of the sepulture or sand warm up, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and let him drink.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the application of medicinal remedies until he is cured, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the arrow, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping up of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have pores in the urethra, or where the pores are small, or are not in their proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it suits him to do so quickly before he passes much very subtle mucus according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then insert or perforate the thin cloth of linen, and secure it in place for three days or four. When he begins to urinate, remove the cloth, allow urination, and then replace it.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance it may not be necessary, for the urine that comes forth does not allow it to remain closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the wound from which the lead is pierced is small, it should be medicated with a lead clove, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the perforation in their place will be unable to urinate, for none are born with the perforation at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis upwards.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot heal because the matter cannot come to the surface, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on their back, then the head of the vein and the cord are also made as thick as a pen, so that the punctures are each in the middle, as it should be.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the bleeding that comes often, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times comes this abscess in the vein, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and among them there are harmful and non-harmful;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	and it is necessary that you pierce them with a sharp needle, and cut and clean them all, then place on cotton moistened with Egyptian ointment;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the ointment diafinicon until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and emitting pus, then you must apply a cauterization to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it, and if the boil is such that it has part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the boil that is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is healed, treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it all together, the head of the boil may not be secured properly, leading to infection and corruption in the boil and around it.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to shave all that is black and corrupted, then tie over the plaster of honey and flour which is made from the bark of pomegranate peels and tares, and cure with other plasters until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery aids in both dispositions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	it is to say, for the bleeding and the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to insert a probe into the head of the penis, and let the patient urinate with it inside.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hair is shaved from the head of the penis which affects those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to scrape the head of the penis with a hooked instrument until the threads are loosened, and release the head of the penis from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if this is a matter to be discussed, you should cauterize it with a spatule for a short while on the head of the penis and the skin.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then separate the parts between two, and place a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water over it, so that it does not dry again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a separation of continuity as are other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	whenever we perform this work of our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the most gentle for their welfare.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have it only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions with forceps, and on an infant, and with a new knife.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if the cords slip because there are two layers, and by chance one of them is cut and the other remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Or if it retracts the cord, and the pain is doubled, and in the healing where it is from the arm, the extremity of the limb is not assured.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and in the healing of the nail, by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs amok, and often they grow thus without needing healing, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the dressing which is done with force on all the thread of hair I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the force cuts just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, cut it equally in one whole thickness;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the threads be well thin between the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if it hears, that you only make him wet the thread between the shaft and then dry it in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	and you make it stretch completely straight, and arrange the forces in your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	and place your hand on the shaft and blow or kiss it, and pull it up until the head of the shaft is tight.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	and clean it well of the filth that is gathered there, then tie the upper part with a double thread, and tie it by one link to another.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it at two points by the second hour at the pocket and the right index, and place between the two joints, then lift the key above quickly and draw the head of the penis;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood drip slowly and slowly, for it is painful.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and apply powder on top and on top of the powder place a cloth glued with one half of a boiled egg soaked in rose water, preserved with good fresh rose oil. Leave it on until the next day, and continue to treat until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces in generation is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	let the shoulders be held and be sharp, and let the shoulder bones also be as large as the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the error of the mundification is when the bowels within are incised;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then you must extend it to your nail, as the leeches do for an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and apply it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, hold it with forceps, and then apply it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they last for three days, and that which is below the scrotum is swollen, let it be until the abscesses are pacified, and then gently scorch it.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	and apply it as you can move it, and be careful not to burn the part of the scrotum, for it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Cure then the limb of sudden wounds from powder, as we have said in treating powders, and if one copes too much of the heart, it goes above, and will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then, as we have said, so that it be healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retain the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to stone passage, or frozen blood, or a bow, or flesh born, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the bladder neck, then it must be treated by raising his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let the feet be placed on the back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constrained for the passage of the stone above, so that the urine is relieved;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringue," of which its form is described here:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it should be made of fine silver, light and feather-like, like the feathers of an eyelash;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let its length be one and a half palm lengths, and let it be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of expelling urine is that you take a double thread, tie at the end a little wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and remove the excess of wool and insert it just to the end of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and seat the patient on the chair, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then lift the penis upward toward the opening.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then insert the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient's urine come from the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order because the way it goes is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then the threads are tied little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then it is extracted and the urine flows;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and continue the suction until the bladder is emptied, and loosen the patient's bowels.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see it discharge acidic fluids and medicines, then make all the instrument called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if at three perforations:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the flax is cut so that the medicines are thick enough to anesthetize well, and if we can remove the moisture and apply when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see your medicines enter the bladder, place the cuspidor in the moisture, and apply what is needed.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you draw out the moisture from there, and then set it firmly.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters there and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle enema with which we enema the bladder:
si est ci:	and it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is made of silver or copper, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and over the heart or the hanging ligaments;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture with which you will enema the bladder into it, then tie it between the two breasts forming a single double thread, and heat that part of the moisture over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	pour le chef du clivert en la verge, puis tienne ta main sur la vessie pour toute la moiteur amenante, tant que le malaide sente que celle moiteur est justement venue à la vessie;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle and pierce it roundly through;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then insert the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a joint, and place within it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder;
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already described in the division the methods of stone, and their extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and we have described the difference between a stone incarcerated by rain, and all the signs, and which stone one should open and treat.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is incarcerated in the bladder often occurs in children, and this is a sign that the urine has become acidic due to its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it passes through the bladder, and greatly afflicts the patient's penis, and it pains him many times, and then diminishes.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and from these jumps the foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and healing is light for children until they are four years old, and very difficult in the elderly, and is moderate for those in between.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the treatment is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it must first cleanse the patient with a clyster to remove all the filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it obstructs at times when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move them into a sitting position, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and passes out through the urethra.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make the patient sit between your hands, and their hands be below their thighs, so that the bladder hangs entirely downward.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then he should probe and touch within;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to incise into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not yield to touching with the index finger of your left hand, soften your middle finger if the patient is pregnant, or your ring finger if the patient is young and fully developed.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and place the stone in its foundation, probe the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, apply pressure at the neck of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press with your finger, and place the stone at the site where you wish to incise.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch the fingers of his right hand upwards, and remove the skin which is beneath the fingers in the part where the incision is made.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then he pours the spatumile copant, which is in the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And he makes the incision between what is between the fingers and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and let it be straight on the stone, and his two hands be close to the fundament, and make the incision through so that it is wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance the press so the dought which is or foundation, she jumps forth without work;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is bone where it has angles and margins:
si est griés a issir;	it is cracked to issue;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if it has a part that is below, resembling a groove, and round, of which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	for those where it has angles and margins, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump, then you must hold it with tongs that are also like a file at the head, to move and extract the bone so that it does not escape.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you pour out from beneath the curved subtle instrument at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot arrange it thus, widen the little hole a bit, and if the wound is without pus, cleanse it with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stone, pour out the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then incise above, then draw it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must sew it up, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or the urine comes down there where the loins cannot close it up;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but in any case strive to treat, or to dilate with forceps, until you treat it piece by piece;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, bind it, and place over it a moist cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then place the patient's head on their neck, and do not remove the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, raise the head of the bone very well with oil and water, then treat with an ointment of defluxicon and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses or corruptions and clots of blood in the bladder occur in the wound, and are thereby retained by the urine, which is known to be in such a manner that it does not flow with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	then thrust your thumb into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder and cause corruption.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cleanse the wound of water and oil and salt, and assist the patient in all ways that you see, until he is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that for all the wounds you treat, you bind his two thighs and apply the medicines to the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is pierced from the genital area, and urine cannot pass;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the treatment of that which I have said so far involves cutting him many times, you are excused from this cutting due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this in such a manner.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I iron fork according to this form and fix it in the fire with three angles.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take a thread and tie it around the genital area below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then push the probe gently into the vein until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the probe in your hand at the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if the urine comes soon, then press your hand on that which is stuck from the stone that is within the vein.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	if it is broken soon, and jumps out with the urine, then the patient is cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, so tie a thread under the stone and another above it, then place the vein against the stone between the two ties, and extract the stone, untie one of the threads, and clean the congealed blood from the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the treatment continue until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	And often there is a need to remove a stone from women, and if it happens even once, the treatment is serious, and it is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	it is one that the woman may be a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that it is impossible to find a woman skilled enough who will reveal herself to the mirrors, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	and the third way is that it may happen that no skilled woman can be found for this art with her hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth way is that the stone in the woman may be more embedded than the stone in the man, which is why a deeper incision is necessary and there is great fear involved. And if such necessity arises for this, you must find a skilled midwife, and at points like these, one must use subtle chaste mirrors.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and it presents a wise dance in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands her to do what you command about the investigation of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and carefully observe whether the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then she must seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, she must hold to her duty, and advises her to perform her duty or examination on the patient, and place and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then incise on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, and let it be such that the stone appears in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his hand over the stone or under it, and cut it at first with small incisions;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then apply the reed to the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound until the stone can exit with force, and know that many kinds of stones exist.
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	this is to know, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with points.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the stone fails to come out, put vinegar in it and hold it for an hour until the stone is dissolved.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is removed, and have with you the tools I told you about in the extraction of the stone from those who assist you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if it flows out, and it is from the artery that has been cut, put the powder on the wound and the bandage of linen and wool, and do not re-open this, and leave the stone untreated, lest by chance the patient die.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is relieved, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Aqua vitae is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white spirits, which come from the heart of the juniper, that contains the essence.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syphac", and sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the skin of the yolk between the white syphac that we have said;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this happens not often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rheum is due to weakness that comes to the embryos, and this material is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from striking the shoulders, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is a yellowish color similar to jaundice, or without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this condition, because if it is white syphac as we have said, it is an abscess, and its size is long like that of an egg, but it does not strike the shoulders, for it has moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, the abscesses are incised with a part of the egg, and because of this it is thought that it is another kind of egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	And if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white yolk, one feels it well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you must probe with the entire intervening square, as its form is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intervening square, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be bled according to our power and the condition of their body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then place the sponge on their back, above something a bit high, and put dust of cloth over him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the patient's heart.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the leit spatium and cut the skin of the patient's heart lengthwise from above the knife until below the ribs, and make the incision entirely straight by dividing the skin of the patient's heart down to the white line, and gently cauterize it according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then puncture the white line fully with an awl, and抽取出所有液体，然后插入你的指甲，将白线上方的皮肤撑开。
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the patient's heart, but only the white line.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut out the whole or in pieces by itself the substance of it thoroughly, for if you do not cut it properly, the pus will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the egg jumps during your work, you must reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the surface.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then join the two flaps of the heart incision with one suture, then treat it as other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspensive, fearing the hemorrhage.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut the heart entirely from the suspensive vessels, extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if an ailment is collected in two parts together, know that these are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you treat the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put on the wound moistened wool in rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put on another layer of moistened wool in wine and oil, and place over the two joints, and put on top doubled cloth bandages, and bind it all with the ligature according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	then take two cloth bandages, and fold them in the shape of strips of wool according to this likeness, and assemble them by stitching at the waistband of the trousers, one head of the shoulder above the fundament down to the back, and the other at the part of the arm.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two heads above the two angles, and let all the restriction gather in the loop of the arm.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this branch of the fire cautery is medicated instead of iron branding, and you should use a sharp cautery blade, peel off the skin from the scales, and heat it as we have said, so that the white syface containing the water is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	and take the cautery in this form, and prick that syface with the pins, and brand it with this sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And dip the cautery in all ways that you can, until you moisten it thoroughly.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and make sure that the fire does not touch the eye.
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more valuable;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and during the stopping of bleeding, and instructing that the operations of cutting be performed;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything else prevents you, or an abscess, or bleeding, or other things, then treat what prevents you according to what was previously said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to wait for this operation because of its horror, then perform perforation as I have instructed. And when you are certain by the signs that we have said indicate a watery abscess, then make the patient sit on the raised seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	 pierced the abscess at the part opposite to the entire spinal column, and make the perforation along the length of the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the wounds be wide so that all the blood may flow freely;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then place cotton on the vein, and bind it, and let the remaining blood flow out, then treat the wound until it is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not allow the blood to flow out through the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a quill or the instrument used to treat blood in hydroptic conditions, as its form is described earlier.
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and widen the wound, and know that the blood will return, and gather after six months or so. And when it has gathered as described before, then the patient's days will pass without issue.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in this branch of the section there is much to fear in various positions, which is why it seems to me that one should beware.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the procedure and similar characteristics of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	Therefore, I say that many abscesses come from flesh, and especially from wounds;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This means that it comes from bitter and acrid superfluity, which is spread in wounds, or by percussion.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the flesh.
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and if he does not find any pain, and there is an abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance it is an abscess with green and yellowish color, and sometimes comes from a vein, or swell due to a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a vein, it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess; when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not fitting that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	The one that is caused by swelling of the vein is known by its arrangement in the expression when touched with your fingers, and can well be incised based on this appearance, and on other symptoms.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you take the heart of the joints, then place the egg on top, and stretch the white evenly, and release the suspender from all sides of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already hardened with these cords, then you must stretch the egg, and take it out;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is air in the white, or within the vessels, then you must release all that tension, and take it out completely.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birthplace of the flesh is open behind, it must be cut out completely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, dress the wound with moistened wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bourjoon, with the joints being softened, and the patient suddenly experiences great pain when it moves.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment for this disease is well prepared like the one mentioned before, and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It must be that you seat the patient on an elevated chair, then put the suspensory ligament of the testicles above your two thighs, at all the vessels near the penis, and carefully stretch them forth.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then incise the sharp-bladed spatula wide across the vessels, until they are exposed, and then brand from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle with double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein has come out, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then incise them straight in the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt fluids.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as with others or with honey, so that no vein becomes inflamed that nourishes either of the joints;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for if this happens, there is no harm, and since all the veins become inflamed, it must be treated in all the veins;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to incising the veins, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syphax
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrences of this branch are due to the section that comes from syphilis, or extension on the abdomen in the region of the inguinal area, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the joints;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either from syphilis, or from the extension of it, and come from these two types of cause:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or by percussion, or by jumping, or by lifting a heavy burden, or by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is due to the extension of the syphilis, are that they occur little by little, over a long period of time, and do not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal until near the fundament, because syphilis presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the ileum, that it causes a sudden onset of pain, and various abscesses appear beneath the skin, for the discharge of the intestine and the body below the ileum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the cicatrices with the intestine are retained inquisitively, and cause great pain to the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron causing fear, for which it is advisable to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to warm the intestines with his hand from within through the wound, if it can enter.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then bind it around his neck. Between your hands, lift the thighs.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then the heart is above, and scrape all the skin from the roots long;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then insert into the flaps of the side inches as you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the intestines may freely protrude.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then cauterize the buttock beneath the skin, until the white fat is completely exposed from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then insert your index finger where the buttock follows, between the white fat beneath the skin of the egg, and between the second layer of fat, and separate what is behind the egg and between the second layer of fat.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move your right hand inside the buttock, and place the white fat on top with your left hand, and lift the egg towards all the fat towards the side.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to extend the egg upward, and untie those that are behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and if there is any part of the intestine exposed or white fat, and if you find any such thing, put it back into the abdomen;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle with a thick thread made of several strands, and sew it in the rear part of the fat, which is after the skin of the hips;
