et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the patient for bodily washing with soluble medicines for putrid humors, and beware of meats that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I see what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and shortly after, the vein swell up as if by a worm in the shoulder, faster than anything else, as if live silver when it is cut from another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place and pierced into the shoulder, and then a little while after spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she turned inward in the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how it moved in this manner from member to member, for I had never seen this disease proceed in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	In all ways, I wanted very much that the pain move from one place to another, but I did not want it as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a hard core and exposed veins, and because these conditions caused the wind torments to appear.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason for those who are sensitive and have moist bodies and veins opened.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, scrape off the top and underneath hastily, and then cover over until the wind diseases have left their place.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, cure it as those who expel wind diseases, such as bitter pills, and pillbugs, and similar things.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are of various kinds, according to their shapes and the places in which they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is such that some have large points, small ones, and hooked, and fused.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those where there are parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which falls into any member, it falls according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member it moves to, such as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any part of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be wary of the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when none of these bad signs appear, and the arrow is not completely removed, then remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and a swelling arises which is above the brain, is when there is scotomia and stiffness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perchance it is without strength in the nostrils, or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perchance loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and the swelling of the wound appears moist and white, resembling a pulse, and also swells as if scalded by hot water;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign is apparent, keep the wound clean, and extract the arrow if it is present.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes or pierces the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and one feels it as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow moves like the pulses, and brings black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you will doubt that many die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never came out is that without bubbles of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and refreshes himself with cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow strikes in the covering of the foot, it hurts the small bones;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and great suffering and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves the entire limb from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls onto the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound with some undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls onto the belly, and it jumps out leaving some hay through the intestinal tract, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and urine spurts out and flows, the patient feels great pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	The wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the arm, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary bone, spine of the back, femur, and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you would do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his arm at the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I extracted it, and removed the rest beneath the fatty tissue behind the ear, and he was cured without any difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I extracted an arrow that fell into the fatty tissue of the eye beneath the membrane, and the arrow was embedded, and could not be reached except its tip toward the wood, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, made of light iron without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the patient was healed, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And they extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arabian arrow with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I extracted the barbs, and pried open as I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And they extracted an arrow from the man, where it was stuck in his chest or abdomen, and thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after XXX days had passed, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I incised the arrow, closed it up, and extracted it, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow fall or pass through him, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and if the arrow remains inside, and does not change its natural position, nor causes harm to any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if another man has an arrow enter his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remains there causing great pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And extract an arrow from a prince's man that was shot among the straw, and it was slightly inclined to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for the treatment after it was dropped for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I handled it with great subtlety, and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain over his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed on the wound a plaster of atratiferous digestive ingredients, because the wounds did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the wound from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster for three days, and redressed the wound again. The patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose;
et il le me dist.	and he tells them.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive salve to the wound with my fingers as long as it was open, and probed it, feeling the head of the arrow which was rotting away at the site.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted the opening of the wound with this corrosive salve until the head of the arrow became clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and passed well through the ends within four months, and then extracted the arrow by enlarging the wound, using forceps to pull it out from both sides, and it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I continued to innovate and devise methods with instruments until I successfully extracted it with forceps on the seventh day, as described in the form that will come at the end of this chapter. Thus, I restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound healed, and the patient was cured entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I have told you about the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your treatment on what I do not say, for books cannot contain everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the master arrowsmith compares only a very small amount, and on what is present and lacking, finds nine works, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows are embedded in the limbs only according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the shoulder or they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which passed through it or where it entered, is an arrow entering into the muscles, and passed but once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not pass now, let it be until the flesh rots entirely, and allow it to come out.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is embedded in the bone, and cannot come out, let it be so for some days, and change each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will pass. And if it does not pass, pierce through entirely with a sharp needle, until the muscles inside are widened, and then withdraw it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the foramina of the brain, and any of the conditions I have said openly to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if not treated at all, but left until it is equalized after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not pierced deep only into the bone, and does not come as far as the surface, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for several days, then the device for extraction should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be extracted with force, I administer tar ointment, as I have said;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded in the body and cannot be seen, then seek it with all means.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, draw it with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot do it due to the narrowness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, widen the wound so that the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has feathers that it holds onto, remove the flesh that is stuck on both sides of the feather that you can reach, and then break or bend the feathers of the arrow so that you can extract it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully ensure that you do not break the arrow, so that you can extract it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it remain until the joint is rotten, then remove it, for the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes it contrary, administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and place something as you can to easily draw the arrow without danger, or soon or late, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck, for this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you cannot, then align him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, or where it penetrates any part of the body, or the skin is swollen so that one can see or feel it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Raise the tweezers up, as far as they can grasp, and then extract:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it should now jump out.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then restart the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, pull it out completely;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft has fallen and you see that it must be extracted, then use the hooked instrument to administer the pull, so that the point of the arrow enters the hook of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then extract it completely, and if the arrow is hooked, use the instrument at the point entering it to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touching, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls or pierces in the belly or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can cut open, then you must cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound if skill is needed.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways about this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the feathered rod is similar to the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, as shown in the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for pressing and knowing this is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins through which one draws blood, there are thirty-one, of which sixteen are principal, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two bumps that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the temples apparent;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that runs along the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the root of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two glands that are in the throat;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins through which we commonly bleed are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fascia," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilica veins, and they call it "vein of the heart.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the fosse, and it is the one through which we bleed, which opens clearly above the pit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the vein called the radial is between the thumb and the ring finger, and it has two sinuses;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg or foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the left pocket, and the second is sophene, which is on the right ankle;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nese," which is in the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The sinew of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the healthier part, as I tell you, and it is that you reset the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then bind the patient's neck with a screw, so that the two veins behind the ears are visible in two places dependent on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	place your thumb there, and where you feel the pulse beneath your thumb, cut there.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancette, and make the incision from below the vein to the bone, then lift your hand above the entire length of the vein, and cut through the skin and vein thoroughly in two depths, and let the blood flow out until you see it.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then extract and bind, while she is sound;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for migraines, sore eyes, and long-term blindness, and for tears in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the healing are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient's collarbone is extracted so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse beneath your throat, and then continue with the procedure;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the heart above the vein at your index finger, and place the lancet below, and lift the vein and the flap as you did in two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put on a cloth.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then press it firmly, and hold it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have also spoken of their application and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment of the vein on the forehead is just as effective for the cephalic vein in diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for rheumatism.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur," whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then straighten the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is sound, and only once the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	In any case, it is not appropriate for the flames to be too hot;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and apply the flame in a crosswise direction, for the bone is nearby, and by chance, the flame may burn through when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The health of the two veins that are in the two lacrimal glands helps them, and with headache, and with redness, and with the orbital part of the eye, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that diseases escape them by twisting at any point, as mentioned before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy one, and let its length be a bit long, its width a bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are fine, they might break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let the blood flow as much as you need, and then tie it with thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The health of the vein near the neck is good for water, and for hard scurvy, and for diseases of the face, as in migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient feels pain in his neck, then in his nose when you grasp it with your left hand, and take the fine long flax thread, and insert it between the two nostrils, because the veins do not open well otherwise, and the sweat will begin to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not apply it too strongly, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, because it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two glands helps in the narrowing of the alaina, and in the beginning of mesenteritis, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and estiomenes;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of health are such that diseases remove their roots from both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the masters be on the side of the patient's head, and let the diseases settle on the seat, then heal the vein along a long narrow path, and draw off tempered blood, or as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	and do the same on the other vein, then release the bond, and moderately restrain all the veins, so that diseases do not choke.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it remain until the morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	of the sinew of the glands
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The veins of the lips above help in swelling in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and around the nose and between them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healed state is to sit the patient in front of you and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by these: one is black and by the small black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then prick both of them, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, then prick the largest one from each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, for they are of the same kind.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the disease beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The veins that are beneath the tongue help after the healing of the cephalic vein, and this is due to the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the uvea, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the healing are that the patient feels relief in their hands before the sun, and the tongue becomes light, and look beneath on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then heal both, and do not perfect them too much, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm that are commonly healed are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with pricking all the large flame mint leaves, or subtle olive oil as you hear sharp, and is called "anisil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the martyr's flame is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	and it has need to open the large veins full of visible blood, and those containing much mingled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointed subtle, and is for cleansing thin veins, or where there is thin yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that affect the throat, and the neck, and the eyes, and the abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is fitting for the patient to bleed and to avoid the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he wounds the artery and a hemorrhage occurs, it is fitting to stop the bleeding as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be pricked by the flame, but cut as with a razor.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilique does not open clearly, then you must extract it, and replace it with another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you take out some of it, or you treat with it the vein inserted in the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the wound with the flame razor, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place to treat, then you must extract the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the head of the shoulder, and then bind the arm, and cauterize the vein with flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be sure that you do not injury the artery when you see the head swollen, for it is the artery.
eschui la donques.	use it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulge up high as urine in a child, and the veins are red and fine, know that it is veins of the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hasten then, and place your finger lengthwise, then remove your finger when the vein has stopped bleeding, for this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the limb for the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and for fear, and do not let him move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not cleansed and it pains you, and medical assistance is not present, open the artery if it appears, for the head of the retraction is needed.
et estainche li sans.	and cleanse the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark of flax, cut it open, and take one half and tie it on well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	and if the wound is cleansed, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	and if not, treat it as we have said, using powders that cleanse blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the cauterizations are not suitable for many positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon must be careful beneath the nerve, and if it is too close, and he finds the nerve, and it swells, then the cauterization will not heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you must anesthetize the surgeon with a麻醉剂;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and cut the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it open along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The health of the cephalic vein helps, for it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is better to treat with pressure from olive oil flame or myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, as it does not cross any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	In any case, it is best to choose the lightest vein, and do not harm anything if it needs to be done for the first time, and one should repeat the procedure.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes the eyes swell in some people when it needs to be done for the first time, but it should not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sinew is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know of a physician, is that medicine is not practiced for gain and to preserve health, and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let medicine be performed in one of the three veins that are called:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and the physician should be called at the beginning of spring and autumn, and after eating in winter, when signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and the physician should be called on the first or third day after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The medicine administered for diseases has no fixed hour, but whenever need arises, at any hour and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not advisable to treat children up to fourteen years of age, nor women who have been pregnant for less than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people who have passed sixty years should not be treated either.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wishes to be treated, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he purge the bowels with a light enema, if there is little retained feces, so that the veins do not receive from the intestines the putrefied superfluities harmful to the principal limbs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor is it advisable to treat those who are too full of meat, nor those who are drunk, to the point of being heavily intoxicated, nor dropsies.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one wishes to treat after colic passion, vomiting, and belly discharge, and frequent intercourse in women, and labor, and watching and fasting, and those whose virtue is entirely diminished, or by something of the weapon or of the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly resolve the humors, if the swelling is great, through meats and through beverages and through medications, if you have the power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then by bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtly resolve the blood, and heal the vein near the foot between the third toes as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep him from work, labor, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be bound and joined, and let the healthier be higher than the one being treated, and rub the arm two or three times, then remove the bandage moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the swelling cannot subside.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell, and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the veins with a bit of old oil, then place his left hand over the vein under the area to be treated so that the vein does not dry or burn.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like cords during the procedure, and some are filled with wind or air, such that when you place them near the flame, you must withdraw the flame, as you cannot open the vein in this manner.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the vein is operated on and the wound is too narrow, for this reason it is necessary that the surgeon be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein works the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, begin again slightly below or quickly above that vein, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient feels better, let it be for one or two days, and do not apply a bandage:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	by chance abscesses may come out;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not take a bath, then begin the treatment again if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the hole is small, or the wound is shallow, and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, then fill that hole itself with the flame directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a bit hastily, so that the joints swell;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the joint swollen, do not re-open the wound, and place a bit of olive oil on it, for it lightens the body's blood and heals the oil that is in this joint.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each wound that you treat for veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing makes the joint stiff and sore when it is placed on the joint.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if the blood and pus are subtle when they are too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens often, even when the incision of the vein is small that time, hasten and place above the spot a wet sponge soaked in water and salt with a bit of heat, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the bleeding from the vein has ceased, and if it remains at the spot after a few days without any black or green discoloration, it will not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place above it some substance of aloe or myrrh soaked in cucumber, onion, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often an abscess and appearance arise in the tissue of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Place your hand there, and if you find the area soft upon pressing with your hand, this is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Hear that you should not apply anything of what we have said, for accidentally it could touch the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but apply a dry plaster to harden the area, then continue treating with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the wound is black, let it continue to drain until it turns red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it large, let it continue to drain until it becomes fine.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is fitting for one who is full and strong, and needs an extraction of blood, that we make the wound larger, and let the flamed be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it suits him to be treated less and more often, and one should treat him by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of treatment is safe from hemorrhage and nerve compression, and is better than long or wide treatments.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	and for one whose body requires treatment, it is fitting to give soft bread with juice of pomegranates.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if it is heated, draw off the blood three or four times. And if it has a cold complexion, eat moistened honey syrup before the meal, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it swells on the side, after the discharge of much blood, it must inhale broth of flesh, and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it sees fit to let the arm swell and be injured again, when it is weakened by great swelling, it must be allowed to swell little by little, according to the quantity of its virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever sees fit to let the arm swell after the first swelling, and if it has strong virtue, it must be allowed to swell for seven hours after the first swelling, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one sees fit to be injured on another side, it must be injured on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has much blood in the body which is now heated, and this causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw off a large quantity, and enlarge the puncture so that it heals in the flesh;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then when you satisfy all the conditions for healing, and place your hand on your pulse when it is healed, so that death does not occur in the flesh, and this happens often when the surgeons are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not fitting when you see the arm dislocated, and cause blood to flow a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, that you stretch the arm hastily, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it be until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you prick it with the tip of the flame, until the blood from the wound has ceased to flow, and place a bit of cloth soaked in water on top and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be, and do not compress it, until the abscess is relieved.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the need arises to treat the blood a second time, let it be done in that very vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is treated in place of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method for this healing is that the patient places their hand in hot water until the fingers become red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind moderately, so that the vein appears well, then heal now through the middle, not wide nor long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the punctures be wide, and heal well near the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, place the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not immerse the hand in hot water, for it should be used more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the treatment of the right hand is effective for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and immerse it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein is crooked, and you can feel it completely, it should not cause any pain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not apply it too strongly, for the nerve is closely beside all the flesh, and then place the hand in hot water, if the flesh is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as it needs, put a cloth with oil and salt on the vein to seal it quickly, and do this for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse [likely referring to an abscess or similar condition], and do everything as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The soul's health is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as liver diseases, retention of flowers, disease of the reins, and of the old thighs and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its vein is such that the patient should pour hot water on it and rub it over the vein until it swells, and tie it above the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there flows much lymph.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Clean the wound or larger wound, or at the ankle, where movement is needed.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you clean it at the foot, beware of the nerves beneath, and clean it through as when cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames anise.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the stone cannot come out, put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the cleaner needs it for the first time, reapply it in a slightly different place the second time, because the joints are salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The loins of the sciatic vein are at the ankle, and its stone is worth for pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his cleaning is that the patient enters or bathes in it, and four dozes are drawn above the ankle by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, heal it in all ways that you can, and by passing through it;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and cut it well that you can, for the liver is soft, and it is very difficult to grasp with hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, heal any vein that opens or is on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let the blood flow as much as you see fit, and then untie the ligature, and place cotton and bind it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Suctions are made of horns, or of skin, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and ventilation is performed according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation which is performed without pricking is according to two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is done with all fire, or with fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventilation which is performed by pricking and extracting blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is entirely at the shoulder.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is placed at the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more at the sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction cup below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction cup between the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup on the kidneys;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction cups placed in the arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction cups on the legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction cups on the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction cup does not treat blood from major veins, but only from small veins scattered in the flesh, and for this reason, it does not weaken one much, as we do with the treatment of a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, nor with all fire or sense of heat, in any disease that comes from overfilling, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of diseases we must bleed, or for custom, we shall administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between times.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to bleed, feel pain in the head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for those who experience overfilling and redness in their face, and in their head, and darkness before their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and are spitting blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such who think, and see by signs blood, wounds, deaths, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is between the months, we command them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The health of the muscles and aids to the fracture of the head ... that comes to them, and it is not right that this be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventosation is in the place of the health of the cephalic, and it is not right that those of cold complexion use it, or who have cholera, for it does them much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, it is not right that those who have cold diseases of the head use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who frequently draw blood thus become forgetful, and because of this, it is necessary to place the cupping device a little more downward due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventosation applied to the neck is in place of the health of the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason, it is effective for narrowing the pit, and cutting into the channel of the brachial artery, and at once, and for replenishment.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should not be held too tightly, for if it is held too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The windusations at the second ribs of the neck are for headaches, eye pain, migraines, strangles, and tooth root pains, and are placed in the location of the health of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it must be instructed to the patient that he should expose his hand when placing it, not compressing the artery and avoiding hemorrhages of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The windusations below the chin are for mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar ailments that affect the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in its place for the health of both sides.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind-vasations of the shoulders are for diseases that come from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The opening of the costal veins is equivalent to that of three veins in the arm, as they drain blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the healthy one not to cut too deeply, for the liver is naked of flesh and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass on the buttock is equivalent to hemorrhoids in the pelvis and diseases beneath. It should be large, made of iron, and well-sealed.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it were too thin, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and he makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cups applied to the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are effective for old pains in the kidneys, marrows, and bladder, and reduce swellings;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are placed on the two ankles and on the two feet, and in any case they weaken the body after long use, and bring paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cup is to first ensure it is vacuum-sealed and then attach it steadily. Place it quickly and move it evenly without stopping until you see the area turn red and swollen, and the reddishness of the blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then apply heat, and replace the cups, and observe the arrangement of the body, for some have firm flesh, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to prick only once, and make wide wounds, but somewhat deep;
et suce legierement.	and gently suction.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the abscess is large, it is necessary to prick twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to dilate the way of the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the abscess is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we wish to draw a little blood at a time, we prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish to have much blood, we often begin;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, we pierce it often, and the ends must be that the veins are suddenly pierced, and it is necessary for those with thick skin and hard ones, and who have small pores, that you anoint the eyes of the suction cups with aperient and solutif oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in winter, with mustard oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or some similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsamite oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being cured has flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil on it, but it should be washed after fomentation with rose water, or cold water, or mullein water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from almond, or mulberry water, or sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or from sacred water, or from decoction of angelica or chamomile, or other similar substances;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not fitting to use a suction cup before or during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the suction treatment, and it is necessary that he be warmed when he is to be suctioned and when he is suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch that the one who is being cured is choleric, and if the blood is too cold and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	and it is fitting that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with vinegar, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little, and fat of castrated animals, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has cold complexion, should take syrup of honey, and moderately fragrant wine between old and new, and eat little, and eat small and light birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day he will use the cupping method, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give some men either treacle or mace before or after the cupping, to comfort the principal limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let them be given in small quantities, but it is not good that those who are hot should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are placed without causing injury are those placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and for gout, and on the belly and the mouth and the veins and the hip, because that limb does not suffer injury to the eyes, and one does not apply fire only to attract blood from member to member, as we place them on the nipples when the infant nurses.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to thin the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place suction cups on the belly and on the mouth to alleviate the member;
