et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieves the pain, when there is an abscess or stone, it relieves the abscess by its attractive virtue by chance, or removes the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus she does it when placed upon the liver and upon the bladder when there is retained windiness, and these cups are administered empty to suction only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water or water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be two inches in width and half a palm from the middle with a small perforation in between, as for threading a needle, and made of brass, so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the middle have a cross piece of brass or iron to hold a candle, and let there be both large and small ones according to the diseases and the strength of those who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, and different from thin ones compared to fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must place this suction cup on the same limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the wax flange or linen, and place it inside the suction cup through the rod that is placed in the suction cup, so that the light be at the bottom of the suction cup and not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and let it be at the puncture as we have said, so that when one looks, if there is vapor, and remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the linen in the same way as before, and repeat often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping applied to diseases of the spleen, for all acute conditions, there is no need for a needle or puncture, and it is not administered forcefully when it is full of fluid, and is placed on the limb only.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without needles they are not administered forcefully only in limbs where one cannot put cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on the bare charred areas, such as the elbows or knees, and other similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the suckling is such that when you find without needles in soft clear fluid without damage, you should use them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and they apply a nut in sweet water until they become softened and have nothing in their cores;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then use venous incision and suction cupping, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and place on the bruises;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and fall, if it is possible to place a suction cup, then put one there, for this is not very effective afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the limb off the bed, then wash it very well, and then dry it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is too sore after removing the bruise, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it there, until the bruises are healed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wound is multiplied, put on broken glass, or garlic, and similar things, until it heals;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the wound half of peeled beans, and leave them until they dry out at the wound, it will stop bleeding now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more need of them, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the bandages do not want to stick, rub the wound with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the bandage sticks, and then place them on it. As soon as they smell the blood, they will dry out;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are渗出，你撒上一点捣碎的没药和盐，或灰烬，它们现在就会掉下来。
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear friend, that the remedies in this chapter, they did not see any of the ancient books, nor did anyone read a letter about them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the knowledge has been lost in our land, for I have never found any good ones;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of them, save through the knowledge in ancient books, or because I have studied so much that I have mastered this knowledge, and through experience, and through the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the summary of our words and the chapters where the wise ones place their understanding, remaining on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or twists or wrenching comes to someone, it is necessary for you to hasten to heal the patient on both sides, if anything fails you, such as weakness of body, or illness, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or where the limbs are either too warm, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and should the limbs be cold, this means cold jousts, and meat of fowl and chervil, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of an abscess being hot, or spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient recovers under his former treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient meat that promotes rapid healing or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, peas, and fish, fresh eggs, and good wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And in the case of meat, it represents nourishment and more quickly heals the fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decrepit cannot be properly healed or set according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but if there is no care, reset the broken bone with large tendons that harden and join the limb together, until it enforces as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not completely remove it from his work, and for this reason, he should be nourished with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	And know that the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or the leg, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	And there are fractures that go lengthwise, and others that go across, just like the cuts of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is fracture with wound, and fracture with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And have his instrument for each manner, and his tool proper in the restoration, according to what memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the break of the bone is due to the twisting of the joint, and clearly appears by lifting, and resounds upon pressing with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting and it does not resound upon tapping, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no point of breakage;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or cracking, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit you to move it by hand, then apply medicines that come after this, and then hold it delicately now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that goes in length, and are the two parts of the joint, you must now put them at equal points, so that abscesses may come to life.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come to head, let him leave it for some days until the abscesses are pacified.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then place it evenly on the skin where you can gently and cleanly, know that the restoration of the former is lighter than the restoration of that which has parts.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it, as is fitting after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, support it from two sides, if it is a hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two strings, or one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the injured member are separated, you must reduce them by all means at their roots in the skin where you can, and guard that through your work no injury or pain come to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel well with your hand if you think it is not properly aligned:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it is set beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those who cause an abscess to come by their work with hot incision and contraction on the limb, as we have often wished.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, well restrain the patient so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is so secured that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet at its proper point, and one must place him in such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and see to it that he is placed correctly, so that no twists remain when he is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are varied in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as fingers and toes:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	and it is fitting to wrap them in soft, fine linen cloth;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	If it is necessary to wrap in a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bands encircle the entire large limb and restrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no shifting;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie with light bandages three or four times according to the limb, and hold your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and restrain less, so that the break can move a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and gradually soften the bandage a little, until you reach a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage, and wrap it again around the broken area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part below the break, and restrain it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first paragraph above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the tied-off ligatures of linen or cloth, so that they be entirely equal, then tie all around the bandage, and then place your well-made dressings on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place on top something soothing for the abscess that reduces swelling, and let it be so for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then place them over your dressings, and let them be of half the width of a large cut cane, or of wood used for splints, or of palm leaves, and let them be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it must be that the dressing which one places over the fracture is somewhat larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as is fitting for the member's size or magnitude;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold on the stileths as you did at the first hour, then tie above a suitable thread as in the first time over the breaster;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter here, and less there;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it must be that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in works of those who make their hours from twisted flaxen cords, and that is a great error, for the thread cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two inches of space between each stileth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the shoulders of the needles after the tightening in their sound places, put over them lint or a cloth bandage so that it does not swell.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	And when the wound is burned and the sinews are broken, I will describe the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to tightly bind the needles for all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to apply great strength for seven days or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that is kept at the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring fractures in many dispositions, especially for women and small children, because it is neither too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster restoring fractures and dislocations and torsions:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take З parts of bark and hand, 3 parts of eye and myrrh and gum arabic and mastic, mix X parts;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, mix 5 parts;
alechil VIIII З.;	alcohol IX parts;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into a powder, and mix with honey of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is a good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another manner of plaster that is good for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugat and vismalve, use X З.;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, use 9 З.;
acaice VI З.;	camphor VI З.;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	bottlewort armenian X З., and grind well, and prepare with water or yolks of eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their sockets, and alleviates the pain ensuing, and the cutting and breaking:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new wool, and the marrow in grease and cooked oil, and put it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for alleviating hot abscesses, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way of plastering which heals broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves, and ground them with terrestrial plantain leaves, and make a plaster from them.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the swelling of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of violette, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind them together, and compound with wine, and if the limb is heated, compound with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply a plaster stronger than the first, when an abscess is hard and comes during the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take root of violette, and seed of flax, centaury, Melissa, and hyssop, and chamomile flowers, of each one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salty water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	And Hippocrates states in his book that one should not apply anything on a broken limb to restore strength that cerote made of wax and oil does, and nothing else more, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that one should apply on the broken limb things dry and a little warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of plastering that is good for wounds and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mustard and combed wool of sheep, or bird feathers, and vinegar, and salt, in equal parts, grind them, and make a plaster from it to apply to the place.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then remove the plaster after some time, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor do the bones move from their place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not, remove the plaster with your hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, with restlessness or swelling, then hasten, and release it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and soak it in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a cloth until you are sure of the warm abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and let the pain go away, then resume the fine binding, and a bit of plaster, but do not strain it so hard as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and finely until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is empty and redness and pain and swelling have been removed from all parts, and you need to apply a plaster and bandage, then proceed with it as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, or it does not dislocate after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and even once let it be twenty days, according to what we see, until the fracture heals and brings the joint close to its place.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then apply more constraint than at first, and let it grow its flesh, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb dry more than necessary, know that no healing can occur.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply hot wet compresses, every time you dislocate it, and let the swelling subside a bit.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this work, cut the tendons in the limb, and quickly mend it as the wise fools do, that leave the limb deformed:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is bad, and these works are full of fears, and I see nothing else but to leave it and do it rightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures exist, with various forms, and the causes are predetermined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because there are fractures caused by sword impact, and the gashes cut through the entire bone down to the marrow that is beneath the bone.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and because of this, this kind of fracture is called "hache" (axe).
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the spear pierces the bone from above without piercing it through, and is called this kind of fracture "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and these are the wounds from these two fractures, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a compression break, or a fracture of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar ones.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break nearby, which approaches just to the tissue beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is located in the bone as fine as a hair, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called this kind of fracture "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or some similar thing, and causes a piece of the bone to enter downward, and the swelling is as when blacksmiths strike on cauldrons.
si entre li piere dedens.	and if between the bones inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have or a head with moist bones, such as a child's head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and happens in all these ways of breaking where small pieces are separated as splinters;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all manners of breaks through their subtraction, and by inquiry with tests, and through the corrupt flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known in this way: when the bone is discovered and rubbed over it, black breaks appear.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take heed of the bad symptoms in the patient, and if you see any ill symptoms such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, fainting, convulsions, fever, and the eyes turning outward and becoming red, and other similar things due to various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any terrifying symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractures come first to you, and it is in winter, then you must extract the bone before the fourteenth day after the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must hasten to extract the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh beneath the bone deteriorates, and the accidents as we have said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture comes as far as the cloth that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part in such a manner:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you make an incision in the head of the patient's navr, and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and more over the figure of the wound. And if a flow of blood comes to the exposure of the bone, or an abscess forms, then use the aid that is appropriate, and it is that you fill the head with moistened cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscesses subside, and you are assured of the cessation of bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin beneath the bone to extract, and this is done according to two methods of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you make the incision narrow in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then one cuts a larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly, so that you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, you must pierce it from below, as you make incisions with tenons, not perfectly but so that they do not penetrate beyond the base of the bone. The tip should have a margin or circle above it, so that the tip does not pass beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have more than one, so that each comes to its place of the thickness of the bone, and that you have threads for all tests;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of three kinds of threads:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing through the broken bone is that you place one thread on the bone, and turn to your two assistants until you know that the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then place the thread in another part a bit after, and do this all around. Cut out the space of the bone which is between the perforations more subtly than you can, gently as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand or to any of the instruments you have such as forceps.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware that you do not touch the skull nor the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the displacement which has remained from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be more precise and finer than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if there remain no small bones or any scales, gently remove them with the instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is that which Galien said, which is simpler.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and let it burn very strong, and this is its purpose.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lancet-shaped instrument the one described here in detail.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut entirely from one side, and let the part be divided into two halves, so that the incision is near the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly strikes the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is close to the bone, gently remove it, for it can be removed with great harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then it must be treated by smoothing out that roughness, and removing scales with a fine razor of which you should have various quantities, to apply in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you need to use large razors first and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other fine incisions and subtle breaks, you must act according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not attributed to him who has dedicated his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and immerse it in rose oil, and apply it to the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another linen cloth doubled over two or three times, and immerse it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to weigh down the wound. Then apply the salve over the other cloth, and do not press it too hard so that it touches only the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be thus for one or two days, until the abscess is pacified, then release it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, flour of wheat, incense powder, and arsenic, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make powder of these things, apply it to the wound, and administer further medicines without causing irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is thoroughly clean, neither leaving out the ointment nor allowing pus to form. For when pus forms on the brain tissue, it can flow and cause great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you apply something caustic to the wound, nerves will not be able to withstand it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care, if no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, there is doubt concerning it.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if darkness comes only because of the medicine that has been placed on it, and it has such virtue, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in gum one wad, and apply it to the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound as is proper until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that either both parts of the neck above are broken, or one alone, for these are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it does not cause swelling or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should place your little finger or perforator of the neck, and set the break evenly within your index finger, and into the pocket to secure it, so that the neck regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose and the fingers cannot reach the place, it must be that you set them evenly on the head of a needle somewhat large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the injury is on two sides, do the other side as well, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	and if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is subsided, then apply to the head of the newborn cloths of linen, if the injury is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	or you apply it to the other side, if the injury is there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the cloths be so large that they fill the newborn's pores.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And any restorer should melt the wicks in butter and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem right that they should be made moist in the preparation of a hen's egg, and with flour powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the cast, while the bones are hard, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes use goose quills instead of casts, and if at the sore wrap a bandage, and keep the blistering tool handy, and blow on the patient from among them.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses break during the work, apply a poultice or moist cotton in rose oil, or with a little balsam.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if there are no abscesses, put an ointment on the wound, made of silk flour and incense powder, cooked with a hen's egg, then place light wads over it, and do not tie the bandage too tight.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break in the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments, then close the wound, treating the injured flesh, and joining, as with plasters and ointments suitable for such.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound within the bone, treat the surface, and apply grains of colocynth until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is ruptured but there is no wound open, and the break is only fissured, not broken into pieces like beams inside, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the break is in the right side, to place your index finger in the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the break is in the left mandible, place your index finger from the right hand on the break gently, and fix it with the other hand behind, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is separated into two parts, you should apply an extension to both parts, making them equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a rupture, strain them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place a dressing on the broken jaw and put a double bandage on it.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the dressing a large stiff piece of well-made cloth, or a piece of leather equal in size to the jaw, and fasten it securely to the cheek. Instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the swelling changes, release it on the third day, and then reset what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And apply a plaster with powder from the mill mixed with abundant egg or sinew flour, after you have removed the dressing.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place a light cloth over the plaster, and if the plaster dries out, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until he is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a gangrenous abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, ensure that no piece of the bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	so subtle in removing with instruments appropriate for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with flambes according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these fragments, and there remains none, close the wound if it is large, and apply plasters convenient for this, to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the forcele
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The shoulder fractures multiple times in front of the shoulder, and the fractures are according to three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is fractured and dislocated in two parts, and there are pieces, making it the easiest to reset;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the procedure is when there is a fracture with a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the force of the broken bone;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the arm towards the proper position;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the fracture evenly in its proper position, so that it has neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place a round pad of cloth or wool over the shoulder on the patient. It should be as large as needed.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and hold the broken bone, securing the pad with your hand, so that you can place the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outwards, because it comes from below fully, then it is fitting that the patient lie often on his side, and place under the shoulder a medium pillow, and have the attendants press the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the shoulder be lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then treat the fracture with your two hands, and if you find any fragments, you must incise over it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any protrusion, apply pressure with one of your incisors that you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place it over the fracture, to prevent displacement:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should resemble a spoon, and is not misplaced, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and use two heads, as you can see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the wound you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, close the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt it is a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloths and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come around, I wrap them in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The compression of the bone, when it is painful and due to a cut, is that you apply on the bone a plaster made from mill dust and egg white, and place light stops over it, and put a sphere underneath, if you need it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage of about one palm in width, and place the cloth doubled over the stops, and apply the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a strip about three digits wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang out.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the stele on the blister, and turn the bandage around the neck, underneath the healthy axilla, and underneath the unhealthy axilla;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the blister properly, and clearly see that the stele does not move over the broken bone, then reward it daily, and when the ligatures are loosened, apply the restraint;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and have the patient lie on their back, and when they sleep, place a small pillow underneath the axilla to lift the shoulder upward;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if the fracture of the scapula is realigned by aligning the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it until no harmful accident occurs, for twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then resume the plastering, if you see that he needs it, and hold it steady until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and in fewer for some individuals.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Often it happens that the shoulder breaks or is damaged in the middle, and cannot be fixed without external application;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	so adjust the joint according to the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then apply on the shoulder powder from the mill with abundant egg, and light bandages, and place over a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and thin board, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are movements anywhere on the board, fill those areas with linen stoppers, so that the board dries evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the board does not move in place, and check the knot each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it dislocates, bind it again, and adjust the board if it has moved out of place, and let the patient lie on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, release it, and be sure, because it is not bone that can set lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone tends forward, and not over the heart, cut it out, and do as we have said in breaking the strong ligament to treat hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of breaking the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bones are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but they often break at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends to one side, and the patient feels great pain, and has difficulty walking. Immediately, and by accident, they may vomit blood, and the movement in the broken bones becomes apparent, and everyone can see this well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that if the patient lies often on their back, and you place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and join the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and subtly and evenly adjust all ways that you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then apply plasters and poultices over the fine salt layer or other light substance, wrap it in a cloth, and bind it to the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the thread round on the back, and hold it properly, and reward each hour the cloth, and if it loosens, hold it tight;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to disengage it, due to corrosion or itching that comes there, or pain or abscess, hasten and disengage it, and apply a fresh poultice, and treat what has come in ways of treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the poultice again, and hold it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of the ribs comes only in those large ones behind the back and at the head inside, and they break only because they are fragile.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and we feel well at the inquiry of the wound.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is to place the break equally, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bandage it with a cloth if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is sinking inward, the patient feels great pain and spasm, similar to pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and they apply leeches, and immediately the patient vomits great quantities of blood, which is a serious illness, and the old method involved great skill.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is fitting to administer foods that swell the belly, to drive away the colic.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make those who have not had an abscess come to one.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have had one, let them be cured.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that we put cups on the side to suction strongly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	in any case, there is doubt that the cups will draw the excess fluids to the side due to the weakness in that area.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And if any of you say that we should cover the shoulder with wet wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the duration equal, then it should be treated with the pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone where the ligament is torn, and doubt exists for the patient, it is necessary to incise over the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place something underneath the instrument to prevent leakage.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must incise the bone, and gently extract it, and then stitch the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses continue to come, place moist cloths in rose oil, and apply them to the area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the area as needed for the abscess, and let it lie properly over the rib where it belongs until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be cured or not, observe whether their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many respects, and if they can move and feel well when you hold and prick them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient will recover if proper care is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is sound or not, observe if the flesh is softened, and if the symptoms are in the hands, and on the back, with sudden ventilation and involuntary evacuation.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is felt on the abdomen, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is sooted on its back and he wishes to heal, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is fatal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if not treated properly.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this does not happen to him, it is the lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that if there is a hot abscess, you apply a rose oil or egg yolk oil until it subsides.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone splits, it is necessary to bind it with a cloth.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound if it is large with stitches, and treat it with ointment promoting healing until it is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the humerus", you should hold your left hand's pouch and place it evenly in your right hand as much as you can, then apply the plaster and bandage over it if needed;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then hold it tight, and if there is exposed bone, incise and remove it, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Then it happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it has happened, there will be a slight alleviation at the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and incise longwise, and incline towards the side, and causes pain at the site, as well as swelling of what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand upwards, as long as you are above the burn.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know which are the breaks and their configuration;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is only in the head, set that break equally, as long as it remains in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is along its length, or it inclines inward, you must lie the patient on their stomach so that the restoration of the fracture can be aligned.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it equally, apply a plaster, then place a wooden or copper splint on top, and bind the brace so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and place the head between the ribs, as long as it is in an equal position.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if abscesses form around it, do not touch them, until the abscesses are alleviated, and apply what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it ought to be, if there is no further bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The auxiliary is that which is between the knife and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of the two methods.
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	of which one is that you take a stick of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two heads with two ligatures, and pull them up, seating the patient on the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then he places the broken arm on the stick, until it comes to the armpit, with a crosspiece of wood in the middle, then pulls up any heavy thing or the attendants extend downward;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the broken part equally with his hands until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you place the patient on his back, and tie the hand to the neck, then command two attendants such that one holds the part above the break with both hands, and the other holds the part below the link, extending each to their respective sections.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the ligament below the break, and above the break, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, you should place one end in the middle below the armpit, and the other towards the side, below the break;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and if the break is towards the side, you should place the end gently, without effort, until the break is equal over the bone and over the side;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then set the break equally as it should be, and hold it steady, if no abscesses are present.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses are present, you should not hold it steady for more than seven days, and place wetted linen in oil and rose oil on the abscesses until they are calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then he holds it in place, and the way to hold it in place is that you apply the plaster over the burn, then set the arm on the shoulder support, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the side.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and place the cloth, and hold it in place on the shoulder support, and on the arm, so that the arm remains straight, unless something prevents it or the bone is dislocated.
