Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is dislocated, use a splint, and place over the break a wider and stronger splint than the others, with two fingers' width between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it spans the break by three fingers' width from each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then hold on the flasks, as I said at the beginning of this chapter concerning the breaker, stronger and less by removing.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the base of the flasks and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you set the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, you let it remain tied for seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then examine each of three days the healing, that itching or swelling not arise at the place, or the swellings not be able to come to the limb because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, do not release the bandage after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and keep his hands over his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place over the shoulder joint a cloth well filled with evenly cut wool, and watch each hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the tendons do not become softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if the remedy through the virtue of medicine, and give the meat that we have placed before, in such a manner that the meat be over the deepest veins;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to heal, let it be large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is custom that the shoulder joint and the leg should be replaced after 40 days from then.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must release and administer baths and ointment medications to heal the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and contracted, it must remain to be untied for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile" bone; one is small and is that which follows the pouchet.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is this one that is beneath, opposite the small bone.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance, the large foscile bone may be broken alone, or the small one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small foscile bone is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large bone is broken, the healing is poor, and more severe than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small fragile bone that is broken only, then it should be extended gently and placed evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large foscile bone, it should be held tighter during reduction.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it over the chest, and hold the hand pouch higher than the others, and the little toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient cross their hands on themselves, and the cushion in front higher, so that the patient does not suffer any discomfort.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the minister's arm to the part below his hand, or at the elbow, and others above the other ministers.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the bones evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break into pieces, place each piece in its place. And if there is any detached part that cannot be grasped and restored to its place, cut it out, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And with the knife for wounds, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	if you take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if during the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, cover the poultice with a dressing made of rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and bind I the cloth gently, until the abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wick, and apply the plaster of the powder of the mill with abundant egg, then place the bandages, and let the bandage of the burner be stronger, and a little wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it should have six bandages or arms in various arrangements:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	let the burner be in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold tighter above the burner than elsewhere, and always less by pulling away, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths that are on the wound be soft and moist, and not hard or harsh;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the threads, from which it is drawn, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is necessary to rinse the limb with warm water until the itching is缓解。请继续翻译接下来的句子：Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the binding. If the ligaments have softened and the bones displaced, address as necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the swelling cannot come to the member, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you loosen it a little, and let it be for a few days, until the swelling subsides, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, do not let him lie dislocated for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or in case of need, then place his hands on his neck, and let his shoulders be level, and take care to prevent movement and displacement, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and by chance in XX days, according to the mixtures and combinations of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers, there are few fractures, and there often comes much swelling.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it must be splinted and set straight in front of him equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the board stretched out, and have the attendant extend the broken bones, and set the joints equal, until they are well aligned;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and wafers if no abscesses come, then place a bandage according to the size of the limb;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the broken bone is in the upper part of the sole between the toes, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to hold it against his broken sole;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then wrap it with a long bandage, and let the padding be of cloth as large as the palm of the hand, and wrap it as fits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the foot, it is fitting that you place one istle above and another below on the sole, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie tightly around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the toes.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the broken bone comes to any of our ribs, if it is displaced, set it equal, as fits.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and wrap it with the sole, and if you see that you place a small pad straight to lift the broken bone, and let it not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is on the other shoulder, as in the index or one of the others, set it equal, and bind it with the healthy shoulder that is next.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all together, keeping them still, or you place a splint on it, as one would for a bag.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of a hot abscess, and aid those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and well one can see it when it turns front and back.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is done by binding the ligament above the fracture, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his back, then each minister extends his limb equally.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture has reached the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, place one bandage against the knife, and the other bandage below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And likewise if it is near the knee, then let the limbs extend from the knee, and let there be downward extension;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then place the bone in its natural position with both hands, and then apply the plaster and the bandage, if no abscesses appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside first, then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The healing is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap the burn with a cloth of hard double thickness two or three times, and let the surplus remain, then move the leg until the heels are at the root of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, behind the knee under, and the head of the thread above;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then wrap the leg and thigh with the cloth, place a strip over the burn, and put a strip on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then place eight strips of cloth around the leg and thigh to equalize the compression, then begin to bind in three or four turns around the burn.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go further from the burn, the binding should be less tight.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then examine the two heads of the thread that you have placed between the thigh and the knee, and in the third space above, then return above to the head of the thread, until you see from below.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, until there is no abscess or swelling or any other similar condition.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	and if it does occur, release it and apply what comes next as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are bits of bone that protrude, you should sew them up if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if it cannot be sewn, then you must cut the skin and extract the bone;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat as we have said, until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the thigh is broken when we insert needles, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	in every way, in the restoration done, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or somewhat less or somewhat more, according to the多样性 of constitution。
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groove of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is not merely a crack or hole, but comes about from any wound, and feels like a deep wound.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that we place what is warm on both sides, until it moves as much as possible.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and put a round needle if you need it, and hold it properly. Then restore all the arrangements as we have said in other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar cases.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you apply to each accident what it needs, until they are healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "mustelz" by straight naming, and the other is called "foscile".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and breaks in the same way as it happens in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is equally the same as that of the arm, and the procedures are all the same. And if both bones are broken together, turn the leg in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bone is broken, then turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen clearly.
et torne desoz.	and turn around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then administer extension, and set it equal, and tie the straps equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but in any case, if the fracture is ugly, and there are multiple pieces, the extension should be less and more gentle;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and adjust according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two bands of soft wood that fit around the leg on both sides, and let them be long from the middle of the thigh to below;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them with one band over and under, and tie them in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is well.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and none administer the bark of the long leg, and it is from the elm, and they place the leg to guard against movement, and properly done in the fracture where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the leg each day, to see if there is any new abscess or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the wound be healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones at the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	A the foot no break comes, but in the bones of the foot a break comes sometimes and in the toes much more, and there is strength only with many conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture in the bone of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground as if it wanted to go, and then put your foot on top of his, at the point where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their proper places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply the plaster and ointments on top, and place under the foot a small board for two heads full, then bind to the foot appropriately, then having wrapped it with cloths around, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the two broken, restore them, as we have said for the bones of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then place on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and let it be a bit wider. Then place under the foot that board I mentioned, and bind it appropriately;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place on each bone a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be placed over the head of the table downward the abdomen of the foot, so that it touches well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things that I have said to other breakers, as we have said;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and attend to each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone at the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, make her sit elevated, then incline her towards the back part, and she should be held from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the cavity of the woman's nature with cotton, and put in as much as it can hold.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then release the woman, and gradually raise her back, and then the cotton will come out as it reaches the entrance of the woman's nature, and the bone will return with the tissue.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wishes to urinate, remove the cloth, and when she has urinated, replace it, and thus for seven days or so.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a bladder of berry, and tie a string to the end, and fill the entire bladder with nature.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the string, inflating the bladder until it is full inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the nature will cause the fracture to heal.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cloth, and leave it thus for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the shoulder in man or woman is broken, reset it thus as we have said for the bone of the hip.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these broken parts nearby to him who puts his study and use thereon, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	and the breaks signify in many dispositions the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the vein, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert the vein into it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it with cloth around, and let it be for three days or wrapped, and it will be quickly healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, to be healed now, as our treatments indicate.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is sound, treat it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then proceed to restore the damage at that same hour or on that day, unless an abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess develops, delay the restoration until the next new day, as long as the abscess is pacified. Do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would cause evil accidents to arise.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the uncovered shoulder, it is necessary to place it gently with your hands, extending it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if you do not have the extension, make one with iron, which has seven or eight long prongs, and the width is according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because of this, it is necessary for the doctor to soak three or four [rags], according to what he may need in each treatment of a broken bone;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let them be clean and slightly large, so they do not fold under compression on the limb during your work, and let them be tight in front, and large in the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palanche," which is why the curved heads should be placed on the head of the visible bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and apply it once, until it returns, and let them be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then use a piece of an appropriate instrument, or probe or needle, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then reset what is stuck in the bone due to hardness and small cracks.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do this until it is in its place, then moisten the dressing with wine tincture, and properly if it is so.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not place any ointment or other thing on the wound that it may cause putrefaction and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer herbs when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the surrounding area, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted by the bandage.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times the foolhardy have done so, and caused the patient to die or become corrupted at least once.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the compresses be softer and more supple than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is deep or large, and you suspect that a bad accident may have occurred, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it should not be dressed with cloths.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but envelop it internally, instead of cloths, with hard bandages, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the wound inking at the wound, remove what you have put on for all wine, and apply healing ointment for wounds, as tetralfarmacion and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is set and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be aligned in such a manner that the wound heals smoothly and gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and the wound does not close further, know that there are small bone fragments, for which you must clean the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the shoulder, or any other form of corruption, it must be treated, according to what is stated in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and exposed in the limb, as with the bones of the thigh or shoulder, or other similar large bones, do not set it, for many times death results, but leave it until it decays.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance it may fall after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of blisters that come over the scalding
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, it is a sad sight to see the figure of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance it may not be able to make the limb perform its natural actions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Therefore take care if the fracture is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and other similar substances, so that you use any of these things, or all together, and prepare them with styptic wine, or with an abundance of egg, or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the nose in stoppers, and hold well, and do not release with your hands for days.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocate it again, and repeat with another, until the nodations are removed.
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or hold well on a well-made piece of flannel.
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of flannel is that it removes all swellings on the limbs.
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the nodation has already turned hard like stone, and it needs to be removed, then apply a cloth above, and cut the excess away.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or have it removed by any razor until it is removed, and treat the wound until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and the limb remains weak and delicate,
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	of which one is because it was bound too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bindings, and the nourishment could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of excessive bleeding;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great movements, or not at their proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because there is little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and strengthen his body, until the blood increases in him.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and give him a bath, and provide him with joy and pleasure.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then apply ointment to the limb, so that the ointment attracts to the large ulcer, and frequently wash it with hot water, until the ulcer heals.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is exposed, and the form of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	for do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish people have done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these operations are blamed, and great harms arise, and sometimes death follows.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	wholly, if the nodations and tortures are fresh, it must be treated with hot water, or boiled soothing herbs such as leaves of vismarula, roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and apply a soothing plaster, as well made, and take the vismarula poultice, and cook it with gelatin fat or hemp oil, and apply it on;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or take fat figs, and grind them with colostrum, and similar medicines that quickly alleviate.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodation is removed to be rubbed continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortuosity is hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed with a steelawl, then it must be filed up to the bone, using a fine incisor lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply caution and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it is fitting now to reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	and if one delays, the eyes will swell, and by chance if they are reset with pins in place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	for it is not fitting that one moves it when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times it brings about spam and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	in all cases, when this happens, make the patient lie down, then let them rest until all the abscesses are pacified;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Often it happens that the jaws are dislocated downward, and the dislocations of both sides occur according to two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are somewhat displaced from their sockets, and somewhat softened.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated, hanging toward the ear, and saliva drips from his mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, enveloping his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it often returns to place through natural means.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and thorough, you must reset it quickly, without delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the minister grasps the patient's head, and places his thumb or a cloth in the pocket of one hand at the root of the jaw dislocation in the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other hand should be held steady, to keep it even;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften, his jawbones, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And you place the joint evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reduction is good, especially if it involves both jawbones together, apply hot and oily herbs, gently resetting them.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	nor violently to reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well, soften it by applying moistened cloths made of rose oil and wax, then bind it loosely with soft bands.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, and let his shoulders be between two cushions, so that they do not move neither to the right nor to the left, nor attempt to move their necks, but give them light food until the pains are gone, and bind the jaws.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat lightly, and do not trouble him to open his mouth for eating and drinking until the jaws are well bound and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandible bones cannot be reset to place within an hour and are not fully returned to their sockets, then fevers and stiffness become accustomed, and by chance there may be intestinal paralysis, and by chance vomiting of black bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, know that it is fatal;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and often the one who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate the lower rib within the continuation of the bone and is only dislocated once at the fracture, and one can feel this.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back and stretches his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the head firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then apply the plaster and the bandage, and secure it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the shoulder that is near the cut cannot be reset;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it can, and if it is reset even once, then reset it to its place as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply the plaster and the bandage, secure it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in the same manner, the shoulder of the scapula is brought back when it is dislocated from its place;
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is not dislocated for three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	of which one is that it dislocates at the part of the neck on the outside;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the shoulder blade;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance dislocates above, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not dislocate behind because of the shoulder, and does not dislocate within because of the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often dislocates outward towards the neck, especially in those who have little flesh, because in them it moves quickly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those who have enough flesh, make incisions, and缝合。 (Note: The last word "rentre a poines" does not have a direct English equivalent in this context and seems incomplete or incorrectly written. It might be intended to say "and close" or something similar.)
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men through a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated for this reason.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It must therefore be tested thoroughly until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation occurs when it moves downward towards the armpit, and place a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a depression at the head of the shoulder, and below the armpit at the axilla, as if it were a hollow.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, though not hidden, for you will find it clearly by touch;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is new or when the person is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the attendant lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places their fingers under the armpit, and resets the joint by gently lifting it upwards to its proper place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the attendant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it under.
si venra hastanment.	if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	and if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the patient should be treated with soothing and relieving remedies, such as a decoction of almond tree, fenugreek, and marigold in water, and it should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then dress the patient's back, and place a cloth of medium consistency neither too soft nor too hard under the bandage. Then put the patient's foot on the cloth and tie the shoulder blade securely, and stretch the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and secure the patient's head, so that it does not move downward.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder dislocates again immediately, and if you reduce it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and you should have someone who is larger than the patient present;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and stand upright facing the patient, and place the shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another minister pull the hand of the patient downward towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may add something heavy to him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And you reduce it also in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is that you insert the long poker into the ground, where the head of the shoulder should be as round as a fist, and neither too large nor too small;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed over the patient, but let it have a hood covering its mouth, and the patient being long of the length of the staff;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then it should extend its hand downwards, and the joints will return to their place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return despite all these things we have said, then perform this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take one stick of two arms' breadth and four fingers' width, which has a head rounded to enter perfectly under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie it over the head of the stick with a hood, so that the stick does not burn the patient, then place it under the armpit of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and stretch out your arm above the pole of the long one, and tie the shoulder above the pole, and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm on the step of a ladder of width, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging from another side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the jointure returns to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, in whatever manner that may be, you must place under the armpit a pad of wool equal, then apply the plaster mixed with powder of grindstone, with incense and egg yolk, over all the shoulder and around, then remove the pad accordingly, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and wrap the hand at its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it must eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture or for another reason, it must be treated with three cauteries at intervals, as is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joints do not hold, and cannot lift your arm upward, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joints will never return to their proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is in the buttocks, and the breasts, or rear, is caused by impact, and extension of hands, and is applied elsewhere.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until he is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there is pain in the limb, and delay with movement, the patient should take bath many times until that pain subsides, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	know that the joints of the elbow are dislocated at points, and return to their place at points.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and when it has lost its moisture from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not responded to, for it can be seen clearly and felt clearly;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and has lost its moisture according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy one, you must see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And the joint is stiff, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it in the same manner as with abscesses that come to a head and heal, for if abscesses come to a head and heal, it would be harmful to bring them back.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be reset in every part, especially when it is at the rear.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and causes even greater pain, and by chance it may lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such, when it is thus that one can bring it back, that you extend its limb with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and its arms be spread out, and the hands placed according to the edges around, in front and behind, and place the joint at its socket or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and fixes the root of the palm cut which is displaced.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it will not return to its place, apply strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is such that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with their hands, so that it does not move with the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm in both directions, after you have wrapped it in a long and wide double cloth;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the eye is placed over the joint to smooth the jointure, then apply the grease of any eye until the jointure returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg yolk, and hold the limb steady, and may the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and let it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the jointure is firm in its place, release the bandage, and let it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the jointure is not set well, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and let it so for some days, until it is firmly placed.
puis le deslie.	then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if it feels painful after the repositioning of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and gently rub it, and press it until it subsides.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you place a piece of fatty sheep fat on the joint for one day and one night, then remove it, and let the area be immersed in water or a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it swells, rub the joint well, then place the fat piece on it again, and immerse it in water or a bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this two or three times until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, place moist heated sheep's fat with butter on it and press it in place.
si revenra a sa disposition.	if it returns to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The shoulder joint is particularly dislocated, and the return is light, more so than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	In all cases, it must be reset quickly to its proper place as soon as it is dislocated, whether the joint is swollen or an abscess has formed.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is done by placing the injured hand on a table, extending the minister's hand, and setting the patient's palm over the location of the joint. Hold it until it returns to place.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	In all cases, you must ensure that it is properly aligned;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then place the patient's hand side down on a table for stretching and realignment.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's back of his hand on the table, and the attendant place his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply plaster to incise and drain the abscess, and let it be so until it can resume.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after a few days, then the joint will remain misaligned.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it will not harm the patient as long as the hand remains soft, and cannot grip anything at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then you will know that the nerve is cut, or the artery.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other means to treat it, by chance nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and let it be 5 days, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is any swelling, apply hot liquid grease and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	The fingers of the hand are sometimes dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or in the wrist;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then reset the fingers, and hold them with your hands until they return to place, then support the hand of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then set it straight on the second day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and do not bind it, as we have said, and release it each day, and allow it to move, and bind it at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is tight, and likewise do so, if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do so as you did before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and likewise do so, if it is dislocated in another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no point in treating it, as death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the vomit leaps without will, nor can it be held back, and often a limb becomes softened, or both thighs or both arms.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the spine moves in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which moves at the rear is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the treatment is such that you should remedy if the yellowishness has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there be no cure or healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment with grand words say that it does not bring great profit to all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the yellowishness that comes to the foot, there is no remedy or healing;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and likewise that which comes directly to the two sides, and can only be cured by that which properly comes to the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be extended on his back with the limb in an even position, and have a cloth beneath him, so he does not swell;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then stick a hot poker into the buttocks and the other at the feet, and tie a bandage under the armpits of the patient, and the other at the hips, and the knees, and the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two ministers know the bands, one at the buttocks and the other at the feet, among the two pokers;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and let them be well closed, the poker as we have said, and the minister place his palms on the buttocks firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, take a board of three ells long, and lay it under the wall, and if the patient is on his side, place the head of the board under the wall, then put the middle of the board over the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and place the patient's feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, do it at the joint that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And when you stick two hot coals at the head of the patient's arm from one side, and near the feet with the other, place half a palm length of long pepper between each coal.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each coal hole either the pointed stick or the stake, and let the coals be firmly in the ground, so that they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two coals have one turning coal, upon which the irons turn, and have in two turning stakes small coals of a palm's length, to turn the stake;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then bind the iron between the cheeks to the stake facing the head, and the other iron away from the feet to the other stake, and each minister turns his stake with all the iron, and the master place the spike evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, place a drying plaster with abundant egg, and then the stoppers, and then the stake of a piece of three palms long, that pierced the vein of the fatness and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with an iron as we have said, and use the patient for subtle healing until he is cured.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if any matter comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer soothing and relaxing medicines, with the dosage that we have said above;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes a piece of flax is administered, and sometimes there appears an appearance in the lower spine of the back, and one should take care that it be dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that protrudes, for which one must not have presumption:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	by chance it would bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the shoulder joints only come from dislocations alone, and do not occur in the same way as other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joints of the hip are dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	dorsally and ventrally, and in front and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more dorsally it is dislocated, and only slightly dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of a dislocation dorsally is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee is more open than the healthy one, and the diseased knee cannot bend as far as the healthy one.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the muscle that is affected and swollen from an abscess of heat, because the head of the thigh bone comes into play.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens is that these accidents are contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of him who is in front, are that his leg is well according to fulfillment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	In any case, do not bend the knee in pain, and if one tries to make it move, it cannot, and it retains its urine, and swells the ankles, and when it goes, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom these happen later are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the site below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The remedy for this case of dislocation is that you reset it if the dislocation is old and remains in its position, then there is no need for further treatment.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it should not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, you must hurry to reset the joint, and stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	If it returns to its place, it has no need of further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary to prepare the minister well, and hold the leg firmly with both hands, or at the part that is tied above the knee.
